### RKP Group advancing $190M Four Corners redevelopment — Spitzer and Nicholas buildings in active demolition phase downtown
_Source: 2025-10-21_

The Lucas County Land Bank's board voted in October 2025 to authorize pre-development agreements with RKP Group for the restoration of the historic Spitzer and Nicholas buildings at Toledo's Four Corners — the intersection of Madison Avenue and Huron Street, the only downtown corner where all four original buildings are still standing. RKP Group will have the exclusive right to redevelop both buildings if conditions are met. The $190 million project calls for approximately 400 new residential units — 180 to 200 in the Spitzer building and 200 to 220 in the Nicholas building — plus an active ground-floor commercial corridor across more than 500,000 square feet of historic office space. RKP Group has led several major Toledo projects over the past 15 years, including Standart Lofts, The Berdan, Fort Industry Square, and The Overmyer, collectively adding more than 350 residential units to downtown.

Interior demolition on the Spitzer and Nicholas buildings began in summer 2025 and is expected to continue through spring 2026. More than $5 million in public funds has been deployed for asbestos abatement, roof stabilization at the Spitzer building, and engineering work, with total public investment projected to exceed $15 million by end of 2026. The project benefits from nearly $20 million in state historic tax credits — $9.6 million awarded to Spitzer in June 2024 and $10 million to Nicholas in December 2023. Reconstruction on the Spitzer building is tentatively targeted to begin in 2026, with completion projected for 2028; the Nicholas building is slated for 2027–2028 construction, with a possible 2029–2030 opening. A previous pre-development team (ARK Developments and The Model Group) stepped back in 2025 due to factors beyond their control; the historic tax credits they secured transferred to the current effort.

**Why it matters:** The Spitzer and Nicholas buildings are among Toledo's most recognizable structures and have sat largely vacant for years — a conspicuous gap at the city's most historic downtown intersection. A 400-unit residential conversion at Madison and Huron would double the residential footprint of the existing downtown core and place hundreds of new residents within walking distance of the Warehouse District, Huron Yards, and the Glass City Riverwalk spine. RKP Group is the right developer for this: its track record in Toledo's adaptive-reuse projects removes the execution-risk question that stopped previous teams. The $15M+ in public investment this year — on top of $19M in state historic tax credits — signals that the Land Bank and state preservation programs are fully committed. Watch for the Spitzer financing stack to close in late 2026, which is the real gating event for whether the 2028 completion target is achievable.

**Sources:** [WTOL — New team chosen to lead Four Corners redevelopment in downtown Toledo](https://www.wtol.com/article/news/local/rkp-group-chosen-to-lead-four-corners-redevelopment-in-downtown-toledo/512-35fe1165-d286-42ec-8b58-e376117c9a20) · [13abc — New developer working on Toledo Four Corners Project to revitalize historic buildings](https://www.13abc.com/2025/09/17/new-developer-working-toledo-four-corners-project-revitalize-historic-buildings/) · [13abc — Four Corners project moving forward with new team](https://www.13abc.com/2025/10/21/four-corners-project-moving-forward-with-new-team/) · [The Blade — Interior demolition begins on downtown Toledo's Spitzer Building](https://www.toledoblade.com/local/city/2025/07/28/interior-demolition-begins-on-downtown-toledo-s-spitzer-building/stories/20250723124) · [Toledo City Paper — Significant Redevelopment Plans for The Four Corners in Downtown Toledo](https://toledocitypaper.com/the-city/significant-redevelopment-plans-for-the-four-corners-in-downtown-toledo/)


### Westgate Village North breaks ground — Trader Joe's leads seven-tenant roster at $60M west Toledo development
_Source: 2026-05-14_

Nordstrom announced on May 14 that it will open a 21,000-square-foot Nordstrom Rack at Westgate Village North — the first Nordstrom-brand store ever to serve the Toledo market. The store is scheduled to open in summer 2027. Westgate Village North is a 27-acre retail development at the northwest corner of Central Avenue and Secor Road (3311 Secor Road), developed by Abbell Associates in partnership with the Nikki Group on the former Elder-Beerman site. The Toledo-Lucas County Plan Commission approved the $75 million development in February 2026; the project calls for three to four retail and restaurant buildings aimed at 'new-to-market' national brands.

Nordstrom Rack President Gemma Lionello said the company looks forward to 'being a part of the Toledo community,' while Abbell CEO Liz Holland called Nordstrom 'best-in-class' and the anchor needed to 'bring a first-rate selection' to the west Toledo corridor. No other tenants had been named publicly at the time of the initial announcement.

Mayor Kapszukiewicz and Abbell CEO Liz Holland led a groundbreaking ceremony on June 10 at the Westgate Village North site. The city simultaneously announced the full tenant roster: Trader Joe's (Toledo's first location), Dick's House of Sport, Golf Galaxy, Sierra, Nordstrom Rack, Mission BBQ, and Smoothie King — all either new to Toledo or new to the northwest Ohio market. Also attending the ceremony: Toledo Chief Growth Officer Brandon Sehlhorst, District 5 City Council member Sam Melden, and Washington Local Schools Superintendent Kristine Martin. The total project cost is confirmed at $60 million.

Abbell Associates is partnering with The Nikki Group on an approximately $30 million redevelopment of the adjacent former Elder-Beerman site; additional retail tenants for that parcel are expected to be announced in coming months. No public opening timeline has been announced for either project.

**Why it matters:** Trader Joe's is Toledo's most-requested national retailer — it has appeared on community wish lists for years and repeatedly cited a market size gap as the barrier. Landing it as the anchor of a new-build development, alongside Dick's House of Sport, Golf Galaxy, and five other new-to-market names, signals that Toledo's demographic and income profile finally clears national retailers' underwriting thresholds. The $60M project on the former Sears site converts a long-vacant anchor pad into a full retail block in one move. For the west Toledo corridor — which serves Washington Local, Sylvania, and Perrysburg shoppers — this is the most consequential retail announcement in a decade. Watch for the Nikki Group's Elder-Beerman parcel tenant announcements, which will determine whether the two-site development becomes a unified retail district.

**Sources:** [Nordstrom press release](https://press.nordstrom.com/news-releases/news-release-details/nordstrom-rack-open-new-location-toledo-ohio) · [WTOL — $75M Westgate Village North plan](https://www.wtol.com/article/news/local/75-million-westgate-village-north-plan-up-for-review/512-3f461339-9898-489a-ae84-4cbac055d0be) · [The Blade — Secor Road retail project approved](https://www.toledoblade.com/local/city/2026/02/12/secor-road-retail-project-approved-plan-commission/stories/20260212131) · [PR Newswire — Nordstrom Rack Toledo announcement](https://www.prnewswire.com/news-releases/nordstrom-rack-to-open-new-location-in-toledo-ohio-302770646.html) · [City of Toledo — Mayor Kapszukiewicz Announces Future Tenants of Westgate Village North](https://toledo.oh.gov/news/2026/06/10/mayor-kapszukiewicz-announces-future-tenants-of-westgate-village-north) · [WTOL — It's official: Trader Joe's is coming to Toledo](https://www.wtol.com/article/news/local/its-official-trader-joes-is-coming-to-toledo/512-24753422-ac77-4a93-9137-eec28a9a9a89) · [13abc — Trader Joe's is coming to Toledo!](https://www.13abc.com/2026/06/10/trader-joes-is-coming-toledo/) · [13abc — Toledo breaks ground on Westgate Village North](https://www.13abc.com/2026/06/10/toledo-breaks-ground-westgate-village-north/) · [The Blade — Trader Joe's, Nordstrom Rack to be tenants in new Westgate Village North](https://www.toledoblade.com/business/development/2026/06/10/trader-joe-s-golf-galaxy-to-be-tenants-in-new-westgate-village-north/stories/20260610036)


### Hotel Lorraine: Jefferson Avenue reopens after facade repairs — but foreclosure case against NJ-based owner advances
_Source: 2026-05-19_

Lucas County prosecutors filed a foreclosure motion against Zoeva Tower LLC on May 19, after the New Jersey-based owner accumulated roughly $80,000 in unpaid property taxes across 14 parcels at 1117 Jefferson Ave. — the century-old Hotel Lorraine, closed since 2019. The structural situation escalated that same week: the building's Jefferson-facing brick facade began bowing at the seventh floor, prompting Toledo Fire & Rescue to close Jefferson Street between 11th and 12th streets. The city gave the owner 72 hours to repair the facade or face fines and potential criminal charges.

Zoeva Tower LLC purchased the property for more than $1.1 million in 2023 with a stated plan to convert the 1925-built hotel into 150 residential units under the name 'Zoeva Tower.' That plan has not advanced, and the building's condition has deteriorated to the point of public safety risk. If the owner fails to address the facade and the unpaid taxes, the property will proceed to a sheriff's auction — with a minimum opening bid matching the outstanding tax balance — before year-end. Lucas County Treasurer Lindsay Webb said: 'Having it sit vacant and experience the kind of nuisance problems that it's experiencing isn't doing our community any favors.'

Additional bricks fell from the Hotel Lorraine's seventh-floor facade on the night of June 16, WTOL reported, with Toledo Fire and Rescue reiterating the danger of falling masonry onto the closed block of Jefferson Avenue between 11th and 12th streets. The city continues to wait for Zoeva Tower LLC to make required facade repairs — no compliance has occurred since the 72-hour repair notice issued in May. Jefferson Street remains closed more than four weeks after the initial closure. The foreclosure case continues to advance in Lucas County Common Pleas Court; the next procedural step is a sheriff's appraisal and potential auction date, which would put the property in the hands of a new owner or the Lucas County Land Bank.

Jefferson Avenue between 11th and 12th streets reopened on June 22, 2026 — more than five weeks after Toledo Fire & Rescue closed the block following the discovery of the bowing seventh-floor facade. 13abc reported that the property owner completed required stabilization work, including securing exterior walls, decorative features, and window lintels. A city building inspector signed off on the repairs. The block closure is resolved; the underlying legal situation is not. The foreclosure case brought by Lucas County prosecutors against Zoeva Tower LLC continues to advance in Lucas County Common Pleas Court, and the outstanding approximately $80,000 in unpaid property taxes remain unresolved. The next procedural step is a sheriff's appraisal and potential auction date — outcomes that would put the property on a path toward a new owner or the Lucas County Land Bank.

**Why it matters:** The Hotel Lorraine is a high-visibility downtown landmark two blocks from the government center and visible on Jefferson Avenue — one of downtown's primary corridors. A sheriff's sale would reset the clock on redevelopment by putting the property in the hands of a new owner (or the land bank), which is actually the faster path to re-use than the current stalemate. The pattern is familiar: NJ/NY-based LLCs acquire Toledo historic structures at low cost, propose ambitious plans, do nothing, and eventually become nuisance properties. Each foreclosure that routes a property through the land bank or a competitive sheriff's sale strengthens the city's long-term property-activation pipeline — but the facade collapse risk is the immediate story.

**Sources:** [13abc — Hotel Lorraine faces foreclosure](https://www.13abc.com/2026/05/19/century-old-lorraine-hotel-faces-foreclosure-over-unpaid-taxes-safety-concerns/) · [WTOL — Foreclosure action filed](https://www.wtol.com/article/news/local/foreclosure-action-filed-against-llc-that-owns-hotel-lorraine-property-toledo/512-c0cba540-4e1a-43d5-991b-c96433045bc6) · [WTOL — Jefferson Street closed](https://www.wtol.com/article/news/local/hotel-lorraine-vacant-structural-integrity-bricks-bowing-facade-falling-brick/512-fe42514f-81f6-4b7e-9b2f-2c6aaac74591) · [WTOL — More bricks fall from Hotel Lorraine](https://www.wtol.com/article/news/local/more-bricks-fall-hotel-lorraine-toledo/512-59960209-2f30-4bfb-8e70-2fbbdefb8a9d) · [WTOL — More bricks fall from Hotel Lorraine as city waits for repairs (video)](https://www.wtol.com/video/news/local/more-bricks-fall-from-hotel-lorraine-as-city-waits-for-repairs/512-8675dea1-30d6-4715-b303-9b7f946c0495) · [13abc — Jefferson Avenue reopens after Hotel Lorraine repairs](https://www.13abc.com/2026/06/22/jefferson-avenue-reopens-after-hotel-lorraine-repairs/)


### Tanger acquires Town Center at Levis Commons for $60M — national lifestyle-center operator enters Toledo market
_Source: 2026-05-28_

Tanger Inc. acquired The Town Center at Levis Commons — a 300,000-square-foot, open-air lifestyle center in the Perrysburg submarket of Toledo — for approximately $60 million on May 28. Tanger used cash on hand and available liquidity for the transaction. The center was acquired from Hill Partners Inc., which has managed, leased, and owned Levis Commons since its opening in 2004. The property is 97% occupied, with tenants including Anthropologie, Sephora, Lululemon, Shake Shack, Starbucks, Athleta, Cinemark, Drybar, Ethan Allen, and Arhaus.

Management expects the center to deliver a first-year return of approximately 8.5 percent, with growth potential over time. The acquisition is Tanger's fourth full-price lifestyle center purchase in its current external growth strategy — following Pinecrest in Cleveland (February 2025), The Promenade at Chenal in Little Rock (December 2024), and Bridge Street Town Centre in Huntsville, Alabama (late 2023). Tanger's national portfolio historically consisted of outlet centers; the lifestyle-center acquisition strategy represents a deliberate broadening of its property type.

**Why it matters:** A $60M acquisition by a publicly traded REIT is a category-one signal of market confidence in the Toledo MSA's retail fundamentals — the kind of institutional underwriting that small-shop and franchise operators watch closely before committing to new locations. Levis Commons has long been the Toledo market's strongest open-air center, but Hill Partners is a regional owner; Tanger is a NYSE-listed REIT with national leasing reach, which means the tenant pipeline for Levis Commons just changed. Brands that passed on Toledo because the landlord lacked national relationships now have a more direct call path. For the broader Toledo retail narrative — which is simultaneously absorbing Nordstrom Rack at Westgate Village North and the ongoing question of what fills Westfield Franklin Park — a nationally managed Levis Commons raises the anchor-tenant competition that benefits all Toledo retail corridors.

**Sources:** [BusinessWire — Tanger Acquires The Town Center at Levis Commons in Toledo, Ohio](https://www.businesswire.com/news/home/20260528308138/en/Tanger-Acquires-The-Town-Center-at-Levis-Commons-in-Toledo-Ohio) · [13abc — The Town Center at Levis Commons announces upcoming sale to Tanger](https://www.13abc.com/2026/05/13/town-center-levis-commons-sold-outlet-giant-tanger/) · [Chain Store Age — Tanger purchases Ohio lifestyle center for $60 million](https://chainstoreage.com/tanger-purchases-ohio-lifestyle-center-60-million) · [Shopping Center Business — Tanger acquires Levis Commons for $60 million](https://shoppingcenterbusiness.com/tanger-acquires-the-town-center-at-levis-commons-in-perrysburg-ohio-for-60-million/)


### DeWine signs $3.7B Ohio capital budget — Lucas County lands ~$48.5M for UToledo, arts venues, and community facilities
_Source: 2026-06-15_

Governor Mike DeWine signed Senate Bill 450 — Ohio's capital budget for fiscal years 2027 and 2028 — on June 15, 2026. The $3.7 billion statewide appropriation delivers approximately $48.5 million to Lucas County, anchored by $18.3 million-plus in University of Toledo facilities funding. Rep. Michele Grim reported the total following the Ohio House's final passage of the bill. Northwest Ohio's higher education institutions claim the largest share: Bowling Green State University receives $19 million plus funding for BGSU Firelands; Owens Community College receives $5.7 million; Northwest State Community College receives $4.1 million; Terra State Community College receives $1.4 million.

Toledo's arts and cultural venues receive a meaningful tranche from the bill: the Valentine Theatre and the Historic Ohio Theatre each receive $500,000; the Toledo Museum of Art, Toledo Live Arts, and the Toledo Arts Commission receive additional amounts from a pool totaling at least $2 million for the city's arts infrastructure. The Historic Ohio Theatre — whose restoration has been underway since lightning destroyed its marquee in 2008 — will receive the final capital funding needed to complete the multi-decade preservation project. Community service facilities also benefit: Cherry Street Mission (Mission Point) receives $407,500 and Unison Health receives $400,000 for facility improvements.

**Why it matters:** Capital budget allocations are the state writing the check for the infrastructure on which economic development happens. The UToledo appropriation lands at a moment when the university is positioning its research and innovation capacity as a workforce-pipeline asset for northwest Ohio's data center and advanced manufacturing bids. The arts venue funding matters because Toledo's cultural corridor — the Valentine, the Ohio Theatre, the Toledo Museum — is part of the soft infrastructure that makes the downtown-activation thesis credible to site selectors. A fully restored Historic Ohio Theatre has been a visible preservation gap on Lagrange Street for 17 years; closing that chapter removes a public-disinvestment signal from north Toledo's commercial corridor. Watch for UToledo to publish a facilities capital plan specifying which buildings receive the appropriation, and for the Historic Ohio Theatre board to announce a completion timeline.

**Sources:** [13abc — Northwest Ohio projects receive millions in state capital budget funding](https://www.13abc.com/2026/06/15/northwest-ohio-projects-receive-millions-state-capital-budget-funding/) · [WTOL — Ohio's $3.7B budget proposal includes funding for wide variety of NW Ohio projects](https://www.wtol.com/article/news/politics/state-politics/ohio-capital-budget-toledo-northwest-ohio-projects/512-e6041392-8049-49c2-b0f3-2ba7eafb0f38) · [The Blade — Ohio capital budget includes $5.7M for Lucas County projects](https://www.toledoblade.com/local/politics/2026/06/02/ohio-capital-budget-includes-5-7m-lucas-county-projects/stories/20260602102) · [The Blade — DeWine signs $3.7B capital budget bill](https://www.toledoblade.com/local/politics/2026/06/15/dewine-signs-3-7b-capital-budget-bill/stories/20260615063) · [WTOL — New state funding helps finish the Historic Ohio Theatre restoration project](https://www.wtol.com/article/news/local/new-state-funding-helps-finish-historic-ohio-theatre-restoration/512-7fe1296b-6205-4110-b2c0-fb8ab5088c17) · [Ohio House — Rep. ### The Blade to vacate century-old Superior Street headquarters — another legacy downtown property heads into disposition limbo
_Source: 2026-01-29_

The Toledo Blade will move operations out of its longtime 541 N. Superior Street headquarters — a building that has housed the paper for nearly a century. Block Communications, the Blade's parent company, has not disclosed a move timeline, a destination, or a plan for the Superior Street property itself. The Blade's associate director of events, Heather Pacheco, confirmed the paper will continue to publish through and after the transition. Coverage this week, including a WTOL feature with Newsguild retirees gathering at the building, suggests the move is now in its active wind-down phase rather than a future plan.

The Blade building is one of the largest legacy structures still in active use in the downtown core, sitting on Superior Street between the Vibrancy 19 cluster and the government center. Its disposition pathway is now an open question: a sale to a redeveloper, a contribution to a TCIC-led assembly, a mothball pending demand, or a phased demolition are all in the option set. None of these has been announced or even hinted at publicly.

**Why it matters:** This is a category-one inventory event for downtown. Add the Blade building to a growing list of legacy properties whose next-use decisions will define the Superior/Jefferson/Madison corridor over the next 24 months — alongside the former Health District building (now slated for demolition with state brownfield funds) and the Hotel Lorraine (heading for foreclosure). The Blade property is too large for Vibrancy's storefront-scale tools and not yet eligible for TCIC's Shovel Ready acquisition (still occupied). That means it falls into a gap in the city's current redevelopment toolkit — which itself is the policy signal worth tracking. Watch for Block Communications' first public statement on disposition; that will set comparable expectations for adjacent property owners.

**Sources:** [WTOL — The Blade to vacate century-old downtown HQ](https://www.wtol.com/article/news/local/the-blade-to-vacate-century-old-downtown-toledo-headquarters-operations-to-continue/512-6227f5d2-d90e-4ee5-a11c-c7076ef6b9ce) · [13abc — Toledo Blade to move from Superior Street](https://www.13abc.com/2026/01/29/toledo-blade-move-its-longtime-location-superior-street/) · [WTOL — Retirees reflect as paper prepares to leave historic building](https://www.wtol.com/article/news/local/the-toledo-blade-retirees-reflect-as-paper-prepares-to-leave-historic-building/512-01fc730c-278d-4c3f-9557-f1a9fe9dba7a)


### Toledo Yacht Club steers clear of June 10 sheriff's auction — 160-year-old Point Place club halts sale with late legal filing
_Source: 2026-05-16_

The historic Toledo Yacht Club — a 160-plus-year-old waterfront landmark in Toledo's Point Place neighborhood — is scheduled for a Lucas County Sheriff's sale on June 10, 2026 at 10:00 a.m. via RealAuction. A January 2026 court judgment found the club defaulted on a 2015 commercial promissory note with Croghan Colonial Bank (originally $350,000), leaving an outstanding balance of approximately $263,164 plus 8.25% default interest accruing since 2023. The Lucas County Sheriff's Office received the Order of Sale in April; an appraisal of the property has already been completed.

The club is navigating compounding structural deterioration — roof replacement, dock repairs, stucco and exterior restoration, window replacement, and HVAC upgrades are all needed — alongside the financial default. WTOL's community-focused coverage found north Toledo residents and Councilmember Theresa Morris rallying around the club: 'It's just devastating for our community,' Morris said. Under the sale terms, the auction can be halted if the debt is paid or a settlement is reached before June 10. 13abc and WTOL first reported the situation in May 2026.

WTOL reported June 2 that the club's board of directors announced it expects to finalize a restructuring process before the June 10 deadline, with the board confirming the facility remains open and all scheduled summer events will proceed as planned. The full debt picture is more complicated than the Croghan judgment alone: the IRS has filed five separate federal tax claims against the club covering years 2021 through 2025, which sit alongside the bank judgment in the creditor stack. A restructuring that satisfies all creditors before auction day would halt the sheriff's sale; if the restructuring is not completed in time, the sale proceeds and the auction opens to any bidder who clears the outstanding obligations.

On June 9 — the day before the scheduled auction — WTOL reported that the Toledo Yacht Club filed late legal documents that effectively halted the Lucas County Sheriff's sale. The precise terms and vehicle of the filing were not disclosed; the club had previously signaled that a restructuring process was nearly complete. The June 10 auction at 10:00 a.m. is off. The club remains open and operational, and its summer event calendar is unaffected. The restructuring story is not over — satisfying the full creditor stack, including five separate IRS federal tax claims, will require additional filings and disclosures — but the immediate foreclosure threat has been resolved.

**Why it matters:** The late legal filing resolves the immediate foreclosure threat — the 160-year-old waterfront landmark avoids distress auction and stays in the hands of its membership. But the story is not over: the full creditor stack includes five separate IRS federal tax claims alongside the Croghan Colonial Bank judgment, and the restructuring that produces those filing terms needs to be ratified and documented. Watch for disclosure of the restructuring terms and the identity of any creditor that took a haircut; those details will determine whether this was a community-backed preservation win or a deferral of the underlying financial fragility. Point Place dodged a worst-case outcome today; whether it emerges with long-term stability depends on what the restructuring actually requires the club to do.

**Sources:** [WTOL — Historic 160-year-old Toledo Yacht Club property set for sheriff's sale in June](https://www.wtol.com/article/news/local/historic-160-year-old-toledo-yacht-club-property-set-for-sheriffs-sale-in-june/512-9bfb2fec-e7f3-4edb-b562-d7e55f0ac0e8) · [WTOL — Weathering the storm: community rallies around historic yacht club as foreclosure auction looms](https://www.wtol.com/article/news/local/weathering-the-storm-community-rallies-around-historic-yacht-club-as-foreclosure-auction-looms/512-97a01275-e752-4cb4-8ca1-6155cd6e5d6a) · [13abc — Toledo Yacht Club faces sheriff's sale over defaulted loan](https://www.13abc.com/2026/05/16/toledo-yacht-club-faces-sheriffs-sale-over-defaulted-loan/) · [WTOL — Toledo Yacht Club facing sheriff auction amid loan default](https://www.wtol.com/article/news/local/toledo-yacht-club-facing-sheriff-auction-following-loan-default/512-2956f6f3-591c-482f-b0d6-9b428a817058) · [WTOL — Toledo Yacht Club looks to alter course to stop sheriff's sale through restructuring](https://www.wtol.com/article/news/local/toledo-yacht-club-looks-to-alter-course-to-stop-sheriffs-sale-through-restructuring/512-8c6d9648-ad4a-4b68-8c22-70052eee39eb) · [WTOL — Toledo Yacht Club steers clear of sheriff's auction with late legal filing](https://www.wtol.com/article/life/local-life/toledo-yacht-club-steers-clear-of-sheriffs-auction-with-late-legal-filing/512-e786d427-36ed-4a51-9deb-414d16b3ab2a)


### Toledo City Council extends Flock ALPR contract 8-4 — Toledo renews as Cleveland's cameras go dark June 29
_Source: 2026-06-22_

Toledo City Council held a public hearing on June 22 on Ordinance O-286-26, which would authorize spending approximately $14,000 to extend the city's existing agreement with Flock Group Inc. for portable automatic license plate readers (ALPRs) used by the Toledo Police Department's Real Time Crime Center — the same public-safety infrastructure that was operational during the June 6 Old West End Festival mass shooting. Residents voiced concerns at the hearing about privacy and about which communities bear the disproportionate burden of surveillance under the ALPR program. Toledo police and the Lucas County Prosecutor's Office have argued the cameras are a key investigative tool that help track vehicles linked to serious crimes, identify suspects, and build criminal cases. The Blade covered the debate on June 22; 13abc and WTOL reported the hearing and upcoming vote. The council vote is scheduled for the regular June 23 session.

The Toledo vote comes as Flock ALPR contracts face growing national scrutiny: more than 30 cities have canceled Flock contracts in 2026, and Cleveland's Flock camera network is set to go dark on June 29 after the Cleveland City Council rejected an extension. Toledo's existing ALPR program was authorized in November 2025, when council voted to expand use of portable cameras; the June 23 vote is a one-year renewal at minimal cost. The substantive debate — who controls the data, how long records are retained, how enforcement use is audited, and whether the technology produces racially disproportionate outcomes — mirrors what Cleveland and other Ohio cities have confronted. Separately, a broader Ohio privacy debate has accompanied the national Flock backlash, with several state lawmakers examining whether statewide standards for ALPR use are needed.

Toledo City Council voted 8-4 at its June 23 regular session to approve Ordinance O-286-26, extending the portable Flock ALPR contract for one year at $14,000. The Blade reported that council members voting yes said they would not take investigative tools away from Toledo Police, while simultaneously issuing warnings that the technology must not be abused. Four council members voted no. The 8-4 split is the sharpest surveillance governance divide Toledo City Council has produced in recent years, and it arrives as Cleveland's Flock network goes dark June 29 — making Toledo's renewal a regional outlier. The vote keeps the Real Time Crime Center's portable ALPR capability intact through mid-2027; the next renewal cycle will carry the full weight of the post-OWE oversight debate the four dissenting votes signaled.

**Why it matters:** Flock ALPRs are part of Toledo's Real Time Crime Center infrastructure — the same technology active at the OWE Festival on June 6 and cited by police as a tool in the subsequent investigation. For the economic development narrative, the outcome of the June 23 vote matters in two directions: a continued robust public-safety technology posture is part of the pitch Toledo makes to site selectors, event organizers, and insurance underwriters in the post-OWE environment; but a growing privacy and civil rights record around ALPR use could complicate that pitch if enforcement patterns draw public scrutiny. The national Flock cancel-wave signals that the surveillance-versus-privacy tension is not abstract — it is a governance decision other city councils have made and reversed. Watch the vote split for how Toledo's council reads the post-OWE public appetite for surveillance infrastructure versus civil liberties protections.

**Sources:** [13abc — Toledo residents voice concerns about Flock cameras ahead of council vote](https://www.13abc.com/2026/06/23/toledo-residents-voice-concerns-about-flock-cameras-ahead-council-vote/) · [WTOL — Toledo City Council holds public hearing for concerns over Flock cameras; vote to be held Tuesday](https://www.wtol.com/article/news/local/toledo-city-council-holds-public-hearing-for-concerns-over-flock-cameras-ahead-of-a-vote/512-3e47e3bb-8fd4-42fe-b7c7-c435a1afdb20) · [WTOL — Toledo residents can weigh in on Flock license plate cameras at public hearing](https://www.wtol.com/article/news/local/toledo-flock-camera-public-hearing-license-plate-readers/512-1241d3f3-d21d-4918-802d-0d5dd0e50daa) · [The Blade — Council debates Flock contract renewal as public safety concerns persist](https://www.toledoblade.com/local/city/2026/06/22/council-debates-flock-contract-renewal-public-safety-concerns-persist/stories/20260622077) · [13abc — Toledo defends license plate cameras amid Ohio privacy debate](https://www.13abc.com/2026/06/02/toledo-defends-license-plate-cameras-amid-ohio-privacy-debate/) · [The Blade — Toledo City Council approves Flock camera contract extension in 8-4 vote](https://www.toledoblade.com/local/city/2026/06/23/toledo-city-council-approves-flock-camera-contract-extension-8-4-vote/stories/20260623121) · [13abc — Toledo extends Flock contract for portable license plate readers](https://www.13abc.com/2026/06/23/toledo-extends-flock-contract-portable-license-plate-readers/)


### Ostrich Towne setback: Avestruz closed in November, Italian concept pending — district enters summer on two confirmed anchors
_Source: 2026-05-18_

Avestruz Tapas & Tequila — one of three restaurants previously cited as open at Ostrich Towne — closed unexpectedly in November 2025 after its management team resigned with minimal notice to investors, leaving employees without their final paychecks. Developer Joe Nachtrab stepped in to cover those wages. A sign on the door announced an Italian dining concept from Chef Paul Matthews — who also operates Riverside Barbeque Company — as the planned successor. That concept was targeted for early 2026 but had not confirmed an opening date as of late May.

With Avestruz gone, Ostrich Towne currently has two confirmed food-and-beverage anchors: Molly's Irish Pub and Riverside Barbeque Company. CuriosiTEA Emporium and the Italian concept remain the next expected openings, but neither has a confirmed date. The district enters the Watershed Weekend foot-traffic window (June 11–14) at a narrower tenant base than the spring framing suggested — and with a fourth tenant now overdue.

**Why it matters:** The Ostrich Towne thesis requires enough tenant variety to sustain dwell-time and return visits. Two anchors can hold weekend bar traffic, but it is a thinner summer case than the three-tenant baseline that had been tracked — and well short of the four-to-five-tenant mix needed to lock in daytime visits. The Italian concept, whenever it opens, is the pivotal signal: if Chef Paul Matthews delivers a second concept that works, Nachtrab has a development story that can absorb setbacks and rebuild. Watch for a confirmed opening date and for CuriosiTEA's status before Watershed Weekend.

**Sources:** [WTOL — Riverside BBQ grand opening](https://www.wtol.com/article/life/food/riverside-barbeque-company-opening-date-july-4-ostrich-towne-north-toledo/512-ff3ad4fe-3b93-495e-9ce2-10bd236e7b9d) · [WTOL — Ostrich Towne growth](https://www.wtol.com/article/money/business/small-business/vistula-district-ostrich-towne-growth-businesses-community-restaurants/512-dbe7ba1e-d81f-45e7-8d4c-99256a76d6c6) · [WTOL — Avestruz closes unexpectedly, employees face pay delay](https://www.wtol.com/article/news/local/ostrich-towne-restaurant-unexpectedly-closes-employees-delayed-pay/512-0006993c-f08c-4e5f-82cc-fea82254bdda) · [The Blade — Ostrich Towne continues to draw interest despite difficulties (Dec. 2025)](https://www.toledoblade.com/business/development/2025/12/05/ostrich-towne-continues-to-draw-interest-despite-difficulties/stories/20251201104) · [Ostrich Towne directory](https://ostrichtowne.com/directory/)


### Sehlhorst leads newly constituted TCIC board as Toledo deploys $20M Shovel Ready Sites Fund
_Source: 2026-02-19_

Brandon Sehlhorst, the City of Toledo's Chief Growth Officer, now serves dual-hatted as executive director of the Toledo Community Improvement Corporation — the public nonprofit launched in August 2025 to proactively assemble and prepare development-ready real estate. In February 2026, the TCIC deployed its first major tool: a $20 million Shovel Ready Sites Fund, structured as a bond against the 35-year JEDZ revenue-sharing agreement with Rossford. The fund begins acquiring and clearing strategic parcels — starting with 1400 N. Summit — so employers can 'move quickly and invest here,' in Mayor Kapszukiewicz's phrasing.

The nine-member TCIC board brings together a cross-section of the Toledo EDO ecosystem: Mayor Wade Kapszukiewicz, City Council President Vanice S. Williams, Chief Equity Officer Dr. Tiffany Whitman, and Sehlhorst as ex-officio city seats; with appointed members Tyran Boyd (Boyd & Associates Consulting, minority business representation), Julia Randles (Crane Development, real estate), Metroparks Executive Director David Zenk, Lucas County Land Bank President David Mann, and Matthew Heyrman (Greater Toledo Community Foundation, regional development). Historical precedent from sites like Southwyck, Textileather, and Ironville — which together now generate $114 million in annual payroll and $1.3 billion in capital investment — provides the proof-of-concept rationale.

**Why it matters:** The TCIC board is the first place where the City, the Land Bank, Metroparks, and private real estate are formally at the same table under a single funding vehicle. Sehlhorst's executive-director role makes him the operational hub of Toledo's proactive site-prep strategy — a shift from reactive deal-making to positioning land ahead of demand. The $20M deployment is the first live test of whether Toledo can compete on site-readiness speed.

**Sources:** [Spectrum News 1 — Toledo $20M Shovel Ready Sites Fund](https://spectrumnews1.com/oh/columbus/news/2026/02/19/toledo--20m-initiative-economy) · [WTOL — Toledo announces $20M initiative to support city's economic future](https://www.wtol.com/article/news/local/toledo-shovel-ready-sites-fund-20-million-jobs-housing-growth/512-4cd6c164-7339-4a83-a2d8-420d31c9993b) · [The Blade — Toledo aims to be proactive with shovel ready sites fund](https://www.toledoblade.com/local/city/2026/02/19/toledo-aims-proactive-with-shovel-ready-sites-fund/stories/20260219119) · [Toledo Community Improvement Corporation](https://www.toledocic.com/) · [The Blade — Meet the individuals poised to serve on Toledo's CIC board (Sept. 2025)](https://www.toledoblade.com/local/city/2025/09/03/individuals-poised-to-serve-on-toledo-s-community-improvement-corporation-board/stories/20250903102)


### Heather Cove Villas: 28-unit 55+ development approved for south Toledo with 15-year tax abatement
_Source: 2026-05-28_

Eagle Creek Builders is developing Heather Cove Villas, a 28-unit 55-and-older community on a 4-acre lot at 3322 Schneider Road in south Toledo's Glendale-Heatherdowns neighborhood. The Toledo City Plan Commission approved the zoning change and site plan; the city is supporting the project with a 15-year property-tax abatement. Pre-construction prices start at $229,900 for two-bedroom, two-bath villa-style homes with attached garages, covered porches, and sunrooms. The Blade reported on the project May 28.

The Schneider Road site sits behind an AutoZone, close to Heatherdowns-area shopping, the University of Toledo Medical Center, and Heather-Stebner Park. A private street and on-site parking are included in the plan. Eagle Creek is a Toledo-based homebuilder with an established track record in the local market.

**Why it matters:** 55-and-older housing is one of the most consistently undersupplied segments of Toledo's residential market — and it also frees up existing single-family inventory when downsizers make the move. A 28-unit market-rate development at $229,900 in south Toledo tests whether new construction can pencil without deep subsidy outside the Vistula-Warehouse District core. The 15-year tax abatement signals that the city's residential incentive toolkit is reaching into legacy neighborhoods, not just the downtown investment zone. If pre-sales track well, Heather Cove validates a replicable model for other aging commercial or vacant parcels along south Toledo's Secor-Heatherdowns-Sylvania corridor.

**Sources:** [The Blade — Heather Cove Villas, south Toledo](https://www.toledoblade.com/frontpage/2026/05/28/heather-cove-villas/stories/20260528073) · [WTOL — New senior villas coming to south Toledo to offer more affordable options](https://www.wtol.com/article/life/new-senior-villas-south-toledo/512-0f7659a4-0a9f-45d9-b910-9e085786cdb9) · [WTOL — South Toledo villa development approved by plan commission](https://www.wtol.com/article/news/local/south-toledo-heather-cove-villa-development-plan-commission/512-8cef6620-000d-46c2-b7b1-50d155b75791) · [Eagle Creek Builders — Heather Cove](https://www.eaglecreekbuilders.com/heather-cove)


### Collingwood Green V opens in Toledo's Junction neighborhood — $29M, 75-unit affordable senior building
_Source: 2026-05-28_

Lucas Metropolitan Housing opened Collingwood Green V on May 28 — a 75-unit, $29 million affordable apartment building at 400 Nebraska Ave. in Toledo's Junction neighborhood, designed for residents age 62 and older. The complex is the fifth building in the Collingwood Green series; monthly rents start at $1,050 for one-bedroom units and are capped at 50 to 70 percent of area median income. Utilities — electricity, gas heat, water, trash, and pest control — are included. A full-time Service Coordinator manages monthly programming, transportation resources, and healthcare access for residents.

Funding includes $6.7 million in federal American Rescue Plan Act dollars directed from the City of Toledo and Lucas County, along with federal and state Low Income Housing Tax Credits and Community Development Block Grant funds. Lucas Metropolitan Housing stated it has invested more than $100 million over the last two years in similar housing preservation and new-construction projects across the city. The Blade and 13abc both reported the opening May 28.

**Why it matters:** Collingwood Green V opens three blocks from the eastern edge of the $53M RAISE project area — the 38-block federal redevelopment now in design phase that will reshape Junction and Uptown through 2031. A 75-unit senior building in this corridor adds foot traffic, service demand, and residential stability ahead of the construction wave coming in 2027–2029. It also validates the city's layered housing investment thesis: ARPA dollars, LIHTC credits, and CDBG can deliver new market-quality units at price points Toledo's senior renters can afford without deep per-unit subsidy. Lucas Metropolitan Housing's $100M in two-year investment is the scale that shifts neighborhood confidence, and each opening tracks Mayor Kapszukiewicz's 300,000-resident-by-2045 population goal at the ground level.

**Sources:** [The Blade — $29M housing project opens for Toledo seniors](https://www.toledoblade.com/local/city/2026/05/28/housing-project-opens-seniors/stories/20260531073) · [13abc — New affordable senior housing opens in Toledo's Junction neighborhood](https://www.13abc.com/2026/05/28/new-affordable-senior-housing-opens-toledos-junction-neighborhood/) · [WTOL — Affordable senior housing complex opening in Junction neighborhood to meet growing need](https://www.wtol.com/article/news/local/affordable-senior-housing-complex-junction-neighborhood-growing-need/512-9b495572-4c86-4cf7-aad5-569164c54521) · [Collingwood Green Senior — Who We Are](https://www.collingwoodgreen.org/whoweare)


### Welcome Home Ohio awards $2.15M to Toledo-area housing orgs — City, Land Bank, and Habitat share $26.9M statewide round
_Source: 2026-05-29_

Governor Mike DeWine and Ohio Department of Development Director Lydia Mihalik announced on May 29 that $26.9 million in Welcome Home Ohio grants will be distributed across 57 counties. Three Toledo-area organizations received awards: the City of Toledo received $600,000 to rehabilitate or construct six homes; the Lucas County Land Reutilization Corporation (Land Bank) received $655,500 — $174,000 for property purchases and $481,500 for rehabilitation or construction of five homes; and Maumee Valley Habitat for Humanity received $900,000 for property purchases ($100,000) and rehabilitation or construction of eight homes ($800,000). Toledo-area organizations received approximately $2.155 million of the statewide pool.

The Welcome Home Ohio program supports the purchase, rehabilitation, and construction of homes and is administered through the Ohio Department of Development. The Lucas County Land Bank and Maumee Valley Habitat for Humanity have an established partnership through which Habitat homebuyers can purchase rehabilitated properties with 0% interest mortgages. WTOL reported the northwest Ohio awards on May 29.

**Why it matters:** The Welcome Home Ohio awards land at an inflection point in Toledo's housing strategy — the week after Lucas Metropolitan Housing opened Collingwood Green V and the Port Authority announced intentions to finance renovations at two more HUD-subsidized complexes. The three awards represent three distinct tools operating in parallel: the City deploying direct construction dollars, the Land Bank clearing and rehabbing properties through its acquisition pipeline, and Habitat delivering owner-occupied units at scale with the 0%-interest mortgage model. Together they address the gap David Mann flagged at the Land Bank's 15-year milestone: investors prefer rentals, so publicly-backed programs have to keep pushing homeownership supply. The eight Habitat homes represent eight families converting from renter to owner in Lucas County — the cumulative effect is what moves the needle on the ownership-rate gap over time.

**Sources:** [WTOL — More than $5.5M awarded for northwest Ohio housing projects through Welcome Home Ohio](https://www.wtol.com/article/news/local/ohio/welcome-home-ohio-grants-northwest-ohio-housing-projects/512-f2245899-b37a-4f2a-94fe-c10e455ce4e2)


### Toledo-Lucas County Port Authority moves to finance renovations at Ashland Manor and Covenant House — two more HUD-subsidized complexes entering preservation pipeline
_Source: 2026-05-28_

The Toledo-Lucas County Port Authority's board indicated on May 28 that it intends to finance renovations at two HUD-subsidized affordable housing properties: Ashland Manor (2030 Ashland Ave., 188-unit Section 8 complex built in 1972 serving seniors and low-income residents) and Covenant House Apartments (702 N. Erie St., near the Warehouse District). Both properties are expected to change ownership — likely to a mission-aligned housing entity — as part of the deal, with Port Authority bond financing unlocking the renovation capital. The Blade first reported the planned action May 28.

The mechanism mirrors the Port Authority's November 2025 action on Heritage Village — where a board resolution unlocked $43 million for renovating 191 units in the Vistula neighborhood and south Toledo. The Ashland Manor and Covenant House action follows the same model: Port Authority issues bonds backed by project cash flows, at no direct cost to taxpayers, and the renovation capital is deployed without requiring a city or county budget line.

**Why it matters:** The Port Authority is quietly becoming the primary engine of Toledo's affordable housing preservation pipeline — Heritage Village in November 2025, Ashland Manor and Covenant House in May 2026. Each action extracts a deteriorating Section 8 property from limbo and puts renovation capital behind it through an off-balance-sheet structure that doesn't compete with city operating-fund priorities. Covenant House's location at 702 N. Erie St. puts it within two blocks of the Huron Yards development cluster, meaning the renovation investment will benefit from — and contribute to — the Warehouse District's rising service demand. Watch for the formal Port Authority board resolution and the identity of the new ownership entity, which will indicate whether this is a for-profit or nonprofit preservation deal.

**Sources:** [The Blade — Port authority intends to finance renovations at Ashland Manor, Covenant House](https://www.toledoblade.com/local/city/2026/05/28/port-authority-ashland-manor-covenant-house-renovations/stories/20260528110) · [WTOL — Port Authority approves $43M plan to renovate nearly 200 affordable housing units in Toledo (Heritage Village precedent)](https://www.wtol.com/article/news/local/port-authority-approves-plan-to-renovate-nearly-200-affordable-housing-units-across-toledo/512-1ba02f08-3ceb-4c27-ae61-05992f330c94)


### Lucas County launches LCReady program to pre-certify development sites — aims for 10 in year one
_Source: 2026-04-01_

Lucas County launched LCReady on April 1, a site-certification program designed to eliminate the regulatory guesswork that slows corporate location decisions. The county's economic development team will pre-certify properties of 20-plus acres or with buildings of 50,000-plus square feet — verifying zoning, utility capacity (water, sewer, electricity), environmental assessments, and endangered-species reviews before a prospect ever calls. The county is targeting 10 certified sites in year one; three properties were already identified at launch: a former potential jail site on Detroit Avenue near Alexis Road, and parcels in Oregon and Waterville.

A parallel AI-powered permitting portal is in development to help catch application errors and reduce back-and-forth with the Building Regulations Department. Deputy Lucas County Administrator Matt Heyrman framed the program's purpose: 'One of the things we're trying to do with this program is make sure we can provide that certainty and provide that speed to market.' Commissioner Pete Gerken echoed the urgency: 'The longer it takes to get things done, people get less interested in doing them.'

**Why it matters:** Site selectors eliminate most candidate markets in the first 48 hours — often because zoning or environmental data is incomplete. LCReady compresses that decision funnel by pre-doing the work that usually takes months after a prospect emerges. Paired with JobsOhio's marketing reach, certified sites give Lucas County a credible tool to compete for the facility investments that the region's industrial land base can absorb.

**Sources:** [WTOL — Lucas County launches LCReady](https://www.wtol.com/article/news/local/lucas-county-launches-program-to-speed-up-development-sites/512-67ec7a3c-102a-4ab5-b65e-b545d87a734c) · [13abc — Lucas County starts program](https://www.13abc.com/2026/04/01/lucas-county-starts-program-ease-process-businesses-begin-or-expand/) · [The Blade — County launches site-certification program](https://www.toledoblade.com/business/development/2026/04/01/county-launches-site-certification-program-begins-work-on-permit-portal/stories/20260401119)


### Lucas County Land Bank marks $1B economic impact at 15 years; David Mann pivots focus to Old South End housing ownership
_Source: 2026-04-22_

The Lucas County Land Bank celebrated 15 years of operation in April 2026, with an independent analysis placing its cumulative economic impact at more than $1 billion — generated through nearly 4,500 demolitions and rehabilitation of roughly 900 homes across the county. President and CEO David Mann marked the milestone but immediately shifted the conversation forward: 'The question is, how do we help to convince them?' — referring to private investors who continue to favor rental returns over owner-occupied housing. Mann said the Land Bank's next priority is the Old South End, where a separately announced $1 million coordinated housing pilot (March 2026) already signals movement.

That March pilot, organized through the Old South End Partnership, was backed by the John Henry Eldred Jr. Foundation and The Stranahan Supporting Organization of the Greater Toledo Community Foundation, with Mann's Land Bank as a founding partner alongside Historic South Initiative, LISC Toledo, Maumee Valley Habitat for Humanity, and LadderUp Housing. The Land Bank has designated the Old South End as a RISE (Rebuild, Invest, Stabilize, and Engage) neighborhood. Mann also sits on the Toledo Community Improvement Corporation board, giving the Land Bank a seat at the table for Toledo's broader $20 million Shovel Ready Sites Fund.

**Why it matters:** Mann's $1B milestone anchors the Land Bank's credibility as a deployment platform — and his public challenge on investor incentives for homeownership, not just rentals, names the structural gap that has historically limited neighborhood stabilization outcomes. With his dual role on the TCIC board and his leadership of the Old South End RISE designation, Mann is now a central figure in both the site-prep pipeline and the neighborhood-scale housing agenda.

**Sources:** [13abc — Lucas County Land Bank celebrates milestone as Toledo makes a housing push](https://www.13abc.com/2026/04/22/lucas-county-land-bank-celebrates-milestone-toledo-makes-housing-push/) · [WTOL — Report: Lucas County Land Bank has made over $1B impact in county over 15 years](https://www.wtol.com/article/news/local/lucas-county-land-bank-billion-dollar-impact-in-county-15-years/512-b0cb4e6c-69c0-4ae0-8e81-093f364dda74) · [WTOL — $1M housing initiative aims to revitalize Old South End](https://www.wtol.com/article/news/local/housing-initiative-revitalize-old-south-end-toledo/512-d7d71bd0-5745-473c-8c37-d738316abd93) · [13abc — Old South End Partnership launches $1M housing pilot](https://www.13abc.com/2026/03/19/local-partnership-works-strengthen-foundation-old-south-end/)


### Plan Commission approves 32-lot duplex subdivision on Dorr Street — 64 housing units cleared for site-plan review in Inverness Village
_Source: 2026-05-15_

The Toledo City Plan Commission unanimously approved the preliminary layout for a 32-lot duplex subdivision on a vacant field along Dorr Street near Byrne Road, in the Inverness Village neighborhood. The plan calls for a U-shaped private road tying into Dorr at both ends, with on-site stormwater detention, sidewalks, underground utilities, and fire hydrants. The developer was not identified at the hearing. Detailed construction plans return to the commission for final review before any permits can issue.

At full buildout the project would add 64 housing units to a market segment Toledo has consistently undersupplied — duplex / small-multifamily product in established neighborhoods with intact street grids. Inverness Village sits along the Dorr/Byrne corridor, with proximity to Dorr Street's commercial spine and access to Anthony Wayne Trail for downtown commuting. Watch the pricing tier when units come back for site-plan review: market-rate duplex new construction at this scale would be a meaningful data point about Toledo's residential cost-floor and which household incomes can absorb new product without subsidy.

**Why it matters:** Housing supply is the constraint behind every employer-retention story the city tells, and behind Mayor Kapszukiewicz's 300,000-resident-by-2045 goal in the third-term strategic plan. 64 units in a single approval at Plan Commission is not a Vistula stadium, but it is exactly the kind of incremental supply that the population goal requires at scale. If this project closes and lays foundations on schedule, it sets a tempo other vacant-field sites in southwest Toledo can follow. The unidentified developer is the next data point to watch — that name and its track record will tell us whether this is a one-off or the leading edge of a duplex-build cycle.

**Sources:** [13abc — Plan Commission approves 32-lot duplex development on Dorr Street](https://www.13abc.com/2026/05/15/toledo-plan-commission-approves-32-lot-duplex-development-dorr-street/)


### Michigan-based JVIS acquires Toledo Molding & Die for ~$80M, preserving 629 NW Ohio manufacturing jobs
_Source: 2026-05-15_

A U.S. Bankruptcy Court judge in Houston signed the sale order on May 14, authorizing the transfer of Toledo Molding & Die's Tiffin and Bowling Green operations to TNJ Ohio, an affiliate of Michigan-based JVIS, for approximately $80 million. More than 629 manufacturing workers — whose jobs were threatened when parent company First Brands Group entered bankruptcy — will retain their positions. The acquisition marks JVIS's first manufacturing footprint in Ohio.

JVIS Vice President of External Affairs David Robinson described the deal as 'an important milestone' and said TMD's 'experienced employees, strong customer relationships, and manufacturing capabilities align extremely well with our long-term strategy.' The company said it plans to continue operations at both facilities without interruption.

**Why it matters:** Toledo Molding & Die is one of the legacy automotive-supply names tied to northwest Ohio's manufacturing identity — the 'Toledo' in the brand matters symbolically even though the plants are in Tiffin and Bowling Green. Preserving 629 jobs and keeping the operations in regional hands (via a Midwest acquirer) avoids the supplier-base contraction that would ripple into Toledo-area Tier 1 customers. It also signals that northwest Ohio's automotive-supply assets still attract acquirer interest despite industry headwinds.

**Sources:** [The Blade — Acquisition of Toledo Molding & Die](https://www.toledoblade.com/business/automotive/2026/05/15/acquisition-molding-die-save-600-jobs/stories/20260515090) · [13abc — JVIS buys TMD operations](https://www.13abc.com/2026/05/15/toledo-molding-die-operations-tiffin-bowling-green-purchased-by-jvis/) · [WTOL — Michigan-based company acquires Toledo Molding & Die](https://www.wtol.com/article/money/business/michigan-based-manufacturing-company-acquires-toledo-molding-die/512-a46192b7-06bb-4514-9a3c-0736804d84ad) · [JVIS press release](https://jvis.us/2026/05/15/jvis-acquires-tmd-to-expanding-range-capacity-and-molding-capabilities/)


### Foundation Steel moves HQ from Swanton to Warehouse District, bringing 40 jobs downtown
_Source: 2025-06-10_

Foundation Steel LLC is relocating its headquarters from Swanton to the historic Ohio Plate Glass building at 303 Morris St. in Toledo's Warehouse District, partnering with Mosser Construction in a joint $7.5 million renovation of the 47,000-square-foot, 115-year-old structure. The two companies will operate separately but share the renovated space. Foundation Steel executive vice president Danny Dymarkowski said the renovation is expected to complete within 12 to 18 months of the June 2025 announcement — putting occupancy in late 2026 or early 2027.

The move brings 40 Foundation Steel employees to downtown Toledo, generating approximately $3.3 million in annual payroll. Owner Charlotte Dymarkowski said the company had originally planned to remain in Swanton but called 303 Morris 'the right place to be,' noting the building's river views and the opportunity to reinvest in the city. Mayor Kapszukiewicz cited Foundation Steel's expansion in his April 2026 State of the City address as one of several major investments building Toledo's job base.

**Why it matters:** Foundation Steel (annual revenue $60–65M, AISC-certified) is not a glamour tenant, but it is exactly the kind of high-wage, skilled-trades employer that anchors a district's daytime economy. Forty employees at 303 Morris adds a new anchor to the Warehouse District's northern edge, distinct from the Huron Yards/Erie Street cluster. Watch whether the renovation timeline holds — occupancy by end of 2026 would give the Warehouse District two major office additions (HQ at 28 Erie and 303 Morris) in the same quarter.

**Sources:** [Signature Associates — Historic Ohio Plate Glass building sees new life (June 10, 2025)](https://www.signatureassociates.com/historic-ohio-plate-glass-building-sees-new-life-as-construction-companies-share-space/) · [The Blade — Ohio Plate Glass building, new life for construction companies (June 10, 2025)](https://www.toledoblade.com/business/development/2025/06/10/ohio-plate-glass-building-new-life-construction-companies-share-space-historic/stories/20250609078) · [WTOL — Two construction companies partnering, moving to downtown Toledo office](https://www.wtol.com/video/news/local/two-conscruction-companies-partnering-moving-to-downtown-toledo-office/512-7625d9ce-9be6-41ec-bfc1-6273892d3e89)


### Toledo lands $571K state grant to demolish former Health District building, clear 1.8 acres for redevelopment
_Source: 2026-05-19_

The City of Toledo was awarded $571,342 from Ohio's Brownfield Remediation Program (11th round, part of a statewide $61M announcement) to abate asbestos and demolish the city-owned building formerly leased by the Toledo-Lucas County Regional Health District. The 73-year-old structure requires over $10 million in capital improvements and sits on a 1.8-acre property. The Health District announced in 2025 it would relocate to the Diocese of Toledo's former Pastoral Center, leaving the downtown property vacant.

Chief Growth Officer Brandon Sehlhorst described the award as helping the city 'address a soon-to-be-vacant and functionally obsolete property in downtown Toledo.' No specific redeveloper or redevelopment program has been named for the cleared parcel.

**Why it matters:** Cleared downtown land is scarce and contested in Toledo's current development cycle — 1.8 acres in the government-center cluster is a meaningful parcel. The brownfield grant removes the asbestos/demolition cost barrier that would otherwise keep the property in limbo for years. Watch for what comes next: a surface lot would be a missed opportunity; a structured disposition through the Toledo Community Improvement Corporation's Shovel Ready Sites model would be the right frame. The property address and its walkability to Glass City Metropark will matter when the RFP (if one comes) is written.

**Sources:** [City of Toledo press release](https://toledo.oh.gov/news/2026/05/19/city-of-toledo-awarded-571-342-grant-from-ohio-brownfield-remediation-program) · [13abc](https://www.13abc.com/2026/05/19/city-toledo-awarded-grant-demolish-former-health-district-building/) · [WTOL — statewide brownfield round](https://www.wtol.com/article/tech/science/environment/state-awards-61m-for-brownfield-remediation-in-75-counties-here-are-the-projects-receiving-grants-in-northwest-ohio/512-36f54f6e-7273-4a2c-abff-abe2c2c7e13f)


### Innovation Post tenant slate firms up — four named tenants

The Innovation Post — the centerpiece commercial space inside the $53M RAISE footprint — will initially house four named tenants : Wurtec Incorporated, WorkSpring, Junior Achievement of Northwestern Ohio, and SEGULA Technologies USA. Together they span industrial supply (Wurtec), flexible office (WorkSpring), workforce/education (Junior Achievement), and engineering services (SEGULA — a French-headquartered global engineering firm). City planners separately note that ~67% of Uptown is currently parking lots and green space — the basis for the "extraordinary opportunity for new development" framing during the RAISE design phase.

**Why it matters:** First time the Uptown redevelopment story has named-tenant specificity rather than infrastructure-and-vision rhetoric. Four tenants is enough to start sketching second-order effects — lunch/service demand, daytime population shift, parking absorption. SEGULA Technologies in particular signals to other engineering and advanced-manufacturing companies that Uptown is viable, which compounds. The 67% parking/green-space stat is the political framing developers should expect through 2026 design-phase community meetings.


### Connecting Toledo Neighborhoods to Opportunity — $53M, 38-block redevelopment in design

The federally-funded $53M project covering 38 blocks (13th–21st Street, Adams to Monroe) is in design through 2026, construction 2027–2029, completion targeted 2031. Funded by a $20M USDOT RAISE grant.

**Why it matters:** Biggest neighborhood-scale infrastructure investment in this part of Toledo in a generation. Junction's 45% vacancy rate means infrastructure is going in ahead of private development — a deliberate "build it and they will come" bet.

**Sources:** [City of Toledo — RAISE](https://toledo.oh.gov/raise) · [Toledo City Paper](https://toledocitypaper.com/news/toledo-to-embark-on-redevelopment-project-in-uptown/)

The Toledo-Lucas County Port Authority is pursuing a new warehouse and liquid bulk terminal to expand cargo handling capacity, per The Blade (April 13).

**Why it matters:** Slower-moving than retail news, but the strongest indicator of industrial-side capacity. A liquid terminal signals long-term industrial demand confidence and may anchor downstream logistics jobs.

### TMACOG rebrands as Lake Erie West Regional Council; Toledo City Councilman George Sarantou elected chair
_Source: 2026-01-30_

Members of the Toledo Metropolitan Area Council of Governments (TMACOG) voted January 30, 2026, to adopt a new name: Lake Erie West Regional Council. The General Assembly simultaneously elected new leadership for the year, naming Toledo City Councilman George Sarantou as chair, Lucas County Commissioner Lisa Sobecki as vice chair, and Sandusky County Commissioner Scott Miller as second vice chair. Outgoing chair, Northwood Mayor Ed Schimmel, called the renaming a signal that member communities 'do so as partners in one connected region.'

Executive Director Sandy Spang framed the identity shift as a forward-looking move: 'This new identity represents our intent to expand partnerships, empower connection, and amplify impact across the region.' The council coordinates transportation planning, water quality, and economic development across a five-county NW Ohio and SE Michigan area.

**Why it matters:** The rebranding is not cosmetic — tying the regional planning council's identity to Lake Erie places water-based economic assets (port access, Great Lakes connectivity, waterfront development) at the center of its regional story. Sarantou's election as chair gives Toledo City Council a direct voice in setting the agenda for cross-municipal economic development coordination in 2026.
