### UToledo inaugurates Northwest Ohio Cancer Research Institute — 60+ researchers, $13M in active NIH grants
_Source: 2026-03-03_

The University of Toledo inaugurated the Northwest Ohio Cancer Research Institute on March 3, 2026, at the Health Science Campus. The institute brings together more than 60 cancer researchers — including more than 50 UToledo faculty — whose active work is backed by nearly $13 million in grants from federal agencies, primarily the National Institutes of Health. Dr. Jian-Ting Zhang, a UToledo College of Medicine and Life Sciences professor, serves as inaugural director. ProMedica is among the clinical partners. Working groups are focused initially on breast, pancreatic, and prostate cancers; a biorepository will collect and catalog biological samples and clinical data to support multi-study research.

The institute is the operational anchor for 'Healthy Toledo,' one of three strategic launch pads unveiled by UToledo President Dr. James Holloway. The Healthy Toledo initiative frames the university as a regional public-health asset — clinical care plus education of the healthcare workforce — tied explicitly to improving outcomes in Lucas County.

**Why it matters:** A formalized cancer research institute changes UToledo's positioning from 'hospital with a medical school' to 'research destination attracting federal grants.' The $13M in active NIH funding is the number to track: sustained federal grant performance is what eventually attracts pharmaceutical and biotech partnerships, and those translate into IP, spin-out companies, and high-wage research jobs that stay in Toledo. The ProMedica partnership is the community-facing proof point — it connects bench research to the city's largest health system and to the patient populations in Lucas County that carry disproportionate cancer burden.

**Sources:** [UToledo News — Institute launch](https://news.utoledo.edu/index.php/03_04_2026/university-of-toledo-launches-cancer-research-institute-2) · [The Blade — UToledo launches cancer research institute](https://www.toledoblade.com/local/education/2026/03/03/university-launches-cancer-research-institute/stories/20260303117) · [WTOL — UToledo announces NW Ohio Cancer Research Institute](https://www.wtol.com/article/news/health/university-of-toledo-announces-launch-of-northwest-ohio-cancer-research-institute/512-ec5c1552-6726-47b1-8345-956fc08cf512)


### Dean Monske and RGP land global EV innovation summit's U.S. debut at Toledo's Glass City Center
_Source: 2025-11-11_

Toledo will host EVIS America — the U.S. debut of the Electric Vehicle Innovation Summit — at Glass City Center on November 3–5, 2026, a booking RGP's Dean Monske described as a generational positioning moment. The summit, previously held five times in Abu Dhabi, combines three co-located conferences: EVIS America (EVs), FutureFuelCON (hydrogen), and Mobility TechEX (autonomous and connected mobility). RGP secured the partnership with the event organizer, aligning Toledo's auto-supply-chain legacy with the global transition to electric mobility. Monske stated: 'For decades, Northwest Ohio has powered the automotive industry. Now, as EVIS America arrives, we're proud to open our doors to the world's leaders in EVs, hydrogen, AI, and mobility.'

Mayor Kapszukiewicz framed the booking as consistent with Toledo's industrial identity: 'Hosting EVIS America reflects what Toledo has always been about: hard work, innovation, and building the future together.' The Glass City Center venue — which also hosted the RGP 2026 annual meeting and a series of Owens Corning investor events — is becoming the region's primary platform for national and international economic development signaling.

**Why it matters:** Monske's EVIS win is a recruitment asset as much as an event: landing an international mobility summit brings site selectors, investors, and OEM supply-chain executives into Toledo's orbit on RGP's terms. The November 2026 event is also a live test of Glass City Center's capacity to attract marquee conferences — and of Toledo's ability to position itself as a transition-economy hub, not just a legacy-auto market.

**Sources:** [PR Newswire — The World of Future Mobility Arrives in America: EVIS 2026 Launches in Toledo, Ohio](https://www.prnewswire.com/news-releases/the-world-of-future-mobility-arrives-in-america-evis-2026-launches-in-toledo-ohio-302611911.html) · [WTOL — Toledo to host international electric vehicle summit's US debut](https://www.wtol.com/article/news/local/toledo-host-international-electric-vehicle-innovation-summit-american-debut/512-aa57ba0f-1734-4bd0-a65e-a206d7ec6650) · [The EV Report — EVIS America 2026 Debuts in Toledo](https://theevreport.com/evis-america-2026-debuts-in-toledo)


### Dean Monske and Gary Thompson make the case for hyperscale data centers at RGP's 700-attendee annual meeting
_Source: 2026-03-05_

About 700 regional business, civic, and government leaders gathered at Glass City Center on March 5 for the Regional Growth Partnership's 2026 annual meeting, where RGP president Dean Monske and executive vice president Gary Thompson made a public case for landing hyperscale AI data centers in Northwest Ohio. Monske flagged active misinformation campaigns against data-center siting and said RGP has 'diligently been trying to overcome that misinformation for well over a year.' Thompson, who has led RGP's data-center recruitment effort for four years, told the crowd: 'I have stood in front of hyperscale data centers in the morning, in the afternoon, in the evening, in the sun, in the rain, in the wind, in the snow — they don't make any noise.' The meeting also spotlighted 2025 regional results: 4,895 new jobs, 16,177 retained jobs, and $3.3 billion in capital investments across the 17-county NW Ohio footprint.

The push comes as Meta's $800 million AI-optimized data center in Wood County — RGP's most prominent recent win — is under construction, and as global AI infrastructure spending is forecast to grow from $189 billion (2023) to $4.8 trillion by 2033. The Blade's editorial board followed the meeting with an endorsement of RGP's regional positioning argument on March 9.

**Why it matters:** The annual meeting is the clearest annual signal of where RGP is placing its recruitment chips. Monske and Thompson publicly staking the organization's credibility on hyperscale data-center attraction — and doing so in front of 700 decision-makers — signals that NW Ohio's energy infrastructure and land availability are being actively marketed as AI-economy assets. How many of those pitches convert in 2026–27 will define the next chapter of the region's investment thesis.

**Sources:** [WTOL — Meta and more: RGP seeks to land data centers to meet AI boom](https://www.wtol.com/article/tech/meta-and-more-regional-growth-partnership-seeks-to-land-data-centers-to-meet-ai-boom/512-fbc14c47-e387-48ff-940e-db8c31cad259) · [The Blade — Editorial: RGP makes case](https://www.toledoblade.com/opinion/editorials/2026/03/09/editorial-rgp-makes-case/stories/20260310006) · [RGP — 2026 Annual Meeting](https://rgp.org/rgp-2026-annual-meeting/)


### JobsOhio expands AI Ready Ohio workforce program to Toledo — 3,000+ residents to receive in-person AI certification; UToledo anchors November regional event
_Source: 2026-05-28_

JobsOhio announced on May 28 the expansion of its AI Ready Ohio program to the Toledo market — along with Greater Cincinnati and Columbus — bringing in-person artificial intelligence training and certification to more than 3,000 residents across those three metros. Online training is now available statewide. The program was launched as a pilot in November 2025 in partnership with the Enterprise Technology Association (ETA) and surpassed its original targets, achieving 170 percent of its pilot certification goals. UToledo and Bowling Green State University will co-anchor a Northwest Ohio regional event in November 2026.

The AI Ready Ohio expansion is part of JobsOhio's AI Super Sector strategy, which links Ohio's data-center and AI-infrastructure attractiveness to a demonstrable local talent pipeline. The Toledo expansion follows RGP's $800M Meta data-center win in Wood County and coincides with the region's preparations to host EVIS America (Nov. 3–5, 2026 at Glass City Center) — the U.S. debut of the international Electric Vehicle Innovation Summit that RGP's Dean Monske secured last year.

**Why it matters:** Workforce credential is the second pillar of Toledo's data-center recruitment pitch alongside land and power infrastructure. RGP and Gary Thompson have spent years making the infrastructure argument; AI Ready Ohio provides the talent-pipeline counterpart. A UToledo/BGSU-anchored November event stacks directly against the EVIS America window (Nov. 3–5), creating a two-event sequence that puts the full Toledo AI-economy story — new EV mobility innovation plus AI workforce depth — in front of site selectors and regional economic developers in the same week. Watch enrollment velocity through summer as the leading indicator of whether the Toledo program hits its certification targets ahead of the November anchor event.

**Sources:** [UToledo News — JobsOhio Expands AI Ready Ohio Program to Train Thousands Statewide](https://news.utoledo.edu/index.php/05_28_2026/jobsohio-expands-ai-ready-ohio-program-to-train-thousands-statewide) · [PR Newswire — AI Ready Ohio Expands to Accelerate AI Education and Training Statewide](https://www.prnewswire.com/news-releases/ai-ready-ohio-expands-to-accelerate-ai-education-and-training-statewide-302781343.html) · [Enterprise Technology Association — JobsOhio Announces Expansion of AI Ready Ohio](https://www.joineta.org/blog/jobsohio-announces-expansion-of-ai-ready-ohio-effort-with-enterprise-technology-association)


### Glass City Metropark urban campground — opening 2026

Metroparks Toledo is moving into the build phase on a new urban campground on the East Toledo riverfront, sited between the National Museum of the Great Lakes and the Craig Memorial Bridge, adjacent to the Glass City Marina that Metroparks already operates. The campground will be small but full-service — RV hookups, tent sites, cabins, and a pavilion. Funding stack: a Land and Water Conservation Fund federal grant pays for the access road and campsites; a ~$1M grant from the Lucas County Land Bank (out of $3.2M from the State of Ohio) covers site cleanup. Per Chief Outreach Officer Matt Killam, the campground is part of the broader Glass City Riverwalk project.

**Why it matters:** An urban riverfront campground is an unusual asset for a Midwestern downtown — and boaters from the adjacent marina sharing the pavilion makes for a meaningfully different visitor pattern than Toledo currently captures. It also locks in another contiguous public-investment parcel along the East Toledo riverfront, the next neighborhood in line after Vistula for the Riverwalk-driven private-investment effect. Expect East Toledo land assemblies and small-business positioning to start showing up in the next 12 months.

**Sources:** [Toledo City Paper](https://toledocitypaper.com/tcp-art-culture/metroparks-toledo-is-opening-a-new-urban-campground-in-2026/) · [Woodall's Campground Magazine](https://woodallscm.com/metroparks-toledo-plans-to-open-new-campground-in-2026/) · [NBC24](https://nbc24.com/news/local/metroparks-to-develop-campground-on-east-toledo-riverfront)


### Levitt BLOC Toledo Music Series lineup announced — 12-week free concert run across 4 parks opens July 16

ConnecToledo, in partnership with Metroparks Toledo, the City of Toledo, and Toledo Design Collective, was awarded a multi-year Levitt Music Series Grant through a national public-voting and selection process to run a free outdoor music series at four Toledo parks — Promenade Park, Glass City Metropark, Junction Park, and Danny Thomas Park — through 2026, 2027, and 2028.

The full Levitt BLOC Toledo Music Series lineup was announced June 16, 2026, at a press conference at the Danny Thomas Park bandshell. The 2026 series runs July 16 through October 8, with the first show at Glass City Metropark on July 16. Programming spans gospel, soul, Tejano, punk, hip hop, electronic, and other genres, reflecting Toledo's cultural diversity. All shows are free and open to the public. The series is part of the Levitt Foundation's national BLOC program, which places free outdoor concert series in cities that win competitive grant rounds through community engagement.

**Why it matters:** A three-year programming commitment with venues spanning Junction through downtown is the soft infrastructure that builds cross-neighborhood foot traffic patterns.

**Sources:** [City of Toledo — City of Toledo and Community Partners Announce Levitt BLOC Toledo Music Series Lineup](https://toledo.oh.gov/news/2026/06/16/city-of-toledo-and-community-partners-announce-levitt-bloc-toledo-music-series-lineup) · [WTOL — Levitt BLOC Toledo Music Series bringing free music to local parks](https://www.wtol.com/video/news/local/levitt-bloc-toledo-music-series-bringing-free-music-to-local-parks/512-a855311e-10b5-40b9-91a3-a1208e175654) · [Spectrum News 1 — Toledo announces lineup for new live concert series](https://spectrumnews1.com/oh/columbus/news/2026/06/16/toledo-announces-lineup-for-new-live-concert-series) · [Levitt Foundation — Levitt BLOC Toledo](https://levitt.org/bloc-toledo-oh/)


### Vibrancy Initiative — five-year context for the May 15 awards
_Source: 2026-05-15_

Newly visible in the program-history framing: since the Vibrancy Initiative launched in 2021, it has invested in 100+ projects and leveraged $135M+ in private-sector capital into Toledo redevelopment. The 2026 cycle ($630K pool → 19 projects → est. $13.5M private spend, announced May 15) is on-trend rather than an outlier — the leverage ratio has held in the 20–25× range across cycles.

**Why it matters:** The 22× leverage figure on the 2026 cycle reads better when paired with multi-year context: the city isn't claiming a one-off; it's claiming a repeatable program at scale. If you're modeling future commercial-corridor investment in Toledo, the right base case is "$600–650K of city money per cycle drawing $13–15M of private spend" — and that's the framing the Department of Economic Development is using publicly to justify the budget.

**Sources:** [City announcement](https://toledo.oh.gov/news/2026/05/15/mayor-kapszukiewicz-announces-19-vibrancy-initiative-grant-awards-expected-to-spur-13-5-million-in-investment-across-10-neighborhoods) · [Vibrancy Initiative hub](https://toledo.oh.gov/business/vibrancy) · [13abc](https://www.13abc.com/2026/04/01/toledos-vibrancy-initiative-making-600000-available-local-businesses-revitalize-community/)


### Toledo council approves $5 vehicle registration fee increase 8–3 — SCMR road fund secured through 2028
_Source: 2026-05-21_

Toledo City Council voted 8–3 on May 26 to approve an ordinance raising the city's vehicle registration fee from $25 to $30 per car, meeting the procedural deadline required for the increase to take effect for the 2027 registration year. City administration estimated the additional $5 would generate roughly $1.1 million annually, earmarked for a patch-and-seal program designed to extend pavement life by five to six years. The Street Construction, Maintenance and Repair (SCMR) Fund — the line that underwrites residential and arterial road work — had been running an approximately $1.9 million deficit, projected to go negative by 2028 without new revenue.

The 8–3 vote is decisive. The approval keeps the SCMR Fund solvent through the 2028 planning horizon and avoids cuts to 2027 residential and arterial road projects that city officials had warned against in the run-up to the vote. Toledo joins neighboring cities — including Sylvania, Bowling Green, Maumee, and Waterville — that already charge the full $30 plate fee. The same May 26 council session also approved a new five-year Republic Services trash-collection contract (with incremental fee increases) and rejected, 8–3, an outsourcing agreement for the Toledo Police Department's impound lot.

**Why it matters:** Every economic-development pitch in Toledo eventually meets a road. Road-fund capacity is the unglamorous floor under every site-readiness claim TCIC will make in the next 18 months, every Vibrancy district that needs streetscape work to leverage its grants, and every downtown tenant decision that hinges on whether the immediate street network looks ready. The 8–3 approval resolves the chief fiscal uncertainty in the 2027 road program and keeps the city's maintenance narrative credible. The decisive vote margin means this will not be relitigated — the $1.1M/year line is now locked in through the current council's tenure.

**Sources:** [13abc — Vehicle registration fee increase heads to council](https://www.13abc.com/2026/05/21/toledo-vehicle-registration-fee-increase-heads-council/) · [WTOL — 'We're taxing again': Toledo considers $5 license plate fee](https://www.wtol.com/article/news/local/toledo-considers-license-plate-registration-fee-to-help-road-maintenance-fund/512-95d361bd-41ab-429f-8427-586caff41884) · [13abc — Toledo considers $5 license plate fee for road maintenance](https://www.13abc.com/2026/05/14/toledo-considers-5-license-plate-fee-increase-road-maintenance/) · [The Blade — Toledo pitches additional $5 license plate fee](https://www.toledoblade.com/local/city/2026/05/07/toledo-pitches-additional-5-license-plate-fee/stories/20260507096) · [The Blade — Toledo City Council delays votes on trash, license plate fees (May 12)](https://www.toledoblade.com/local/city/2026/05/12/toledo-city-council-delays-votes-on-trash-license-plate-fees-other-issues/stories/20260512110) · [WTOL — Toledo starts 2026 residential road reconstruction](https://www.wtol.com/article/news/local/toledo-starts-2026-residential-road-reconstruction/512-0f48336c-de55-450d-aca5-0ad707ea0212) · [The Blade — Toledo council approves trash contract, rejects outsourcing police tow lot (May 26)](https://www.toledoblade.com/local/city/2026/05/26/toledo-city-council-approves-trash-contract-rejects-tow-lot/stories/20260526109) · [WTOL — Council approves trash contract with Republic Services, waste fee increases](https://www.wtol.com/article/news/local/toledo-council/toledo-city-council-waste-contract-republic-services-fee-increase-residents/512-a7cd2b9e-2931-481c-8ffd-a3938a0de848)


### Toledo council approves west Toledo water tower permit 9–2 at June 2 special session — $85M project and Kokosing contract cleared
_Source: 2026-05-26_

Toledo City Council voted 5–6 on May 26 against the special use permit needed for two 2-million-gallon water towers planned for Northover Road near Silver Creek Elementary School in west Toledo — the most contested portion of the city's $85 million, four-tower water infrastructure expansion. McPherson, Morris, Gadus, Kramer, and Jones voted against the permit; Martinez, Williams, Komives, Mac Driscoll, Sarantou, and Hobbs voted for it. The rejection pauses the Northover Road work while the remaining two tower sites — Schneider Park on the south side and Holland-Sylvania Road and West Sylvania Avenue — are unaffected.

Kokosing was awarded the contract for the full project, and city officials warned that continued delay risks losing the contractor entirely — which would require a rebid at potentially higher cost. Crews had already begun clearing trees at the Northover Road site before the vote. Council member Theresa Morris, whose district includes the site, has opposed the location throughout: 'I really do feel that my constituents were done dirty, and I think the city didn't do due diligence in looking at other locations.' Nearby residents cited concerns about property values, neighborhood aesthetics, and loss of green space.

Toledo City Council voted 9–2 at the June 2 special session to approve Ordinance 225-26 — the special use permit for the Northover Road towers — reversing the May 26 rejection by a decisive margin. Council members Theresa Morris and Theresa Gadus voted no; the remaining nine members voted in favor. With the permit approved, Kokosing can resume work at the Northover Road site and the full $85M, four-tower infrastructure expansion is back on schedule. WTOL reported the vote result on June 2.

The Arts Commission of Greater Toledo confirmed it is seeking a local artist to create artwork for two of the four new water towers — a 290 by 31 foot painted section on each of the Northover Road (near Silver Creek Elementary) and Schneider Park towers. The call is open to Lucas County residents age 18 and older with a strong vector-based graphic design portfolio; a design review board including Arts Commission and city Water Treatment Department staff will lead selection beginning in July. The public art element signals the project has advanced from permitting to implementation planning, and it provides a community-character layer to infrastructure that has been the subject of neighborhood concern.

**Why it matters:** The 9-2 approval resolves the sharpest near-term disruption risk to Toledo's water infrastructure program. The $85M project is the same utility backbone that underpins the site-readiness pitch TCIC and LCReady make to industrial prospects — data centers, in particular, require stable high-capacity water for cooling. With the Kokosing contract now secure and the permit in hand, the full four-tower expansion can proceed on the original schedule. The reversal from a 5-6 rejection to a 9-2 approval is a decisive margin that settles the question at council. Watch for tree clearing and site work to resume at Northover Road and for construction timeline confirmation from the city.

**Sources:** [WTOL — Toledo council rejects permit for west Toledo water tower project](https://www.wtol.com/article/news/local/toledo-council-rejects-permit-water-tower-project/512-f0a14df1-ddfb-432e-84e5-02f225ab2c7c) · [13abc — City of Toledo to build 4 new water towers, pump station](https://www.13abc.com/2026/04/10/city-toledo-build-4-new-water-towers-pump-station/) · [WTOL — West Toledo neighbors react as construction starts](https://www.wtol.com/article/news/local/west-toledo-neighbors-react-construction-starts-water-tower-project/512-160dc5db-20d1-4f58-82df-d02b6f7f3065) · [City of Toledo — Water Towers at Silver Creek Elementary FAQ](https://toledo.oh.gov/residents/water/water-towers-at-silver-creek-elementary/water-tower-faq) · [WTOL — Toledo City Council to reconsider permit for water tower project](https://www.wtol.com/article/news/local/toledo-council/toledo-city-council-reconsider-permit-water-tower-project/512-7bf0e578-b08d-47f5-8d4a-6bdf603a87b4) · [WTOL — Toledo City Council votes to approve west Toledo water tower project](https://www.wtol.com/article/news/local/toledo-city-council-votes-to-approve-west-toledo-water-tower-project-northover-silver-creek-elementary/512-0a196e27-2304-4710-9caf-a429537a82a5) · [WTOL — Arts Commission seeks artist for Toledo water tower projects](https://www.wtol.com/article/news/local/arts-commission-seeks-artist-for-toledo-water-towers/512-9bdcc382-0c03-4c38-980e-0df112be056d)

### Swayne Field Shopping Center renovation nearing completion in Englewood — $3.6M federal investment targets workforce training anchor and minority-owned businesses
_Source: 2026-05-26_

The Swayne Field Shopping Center in Toledo's Englewood neighborhood is nearing completion of a $3.6 million federally funded rehabilitation, The Blade reported May 26. The 92,000-square-foot, 7.4-acre facility is being redesigned from a car-centric strip center into a walkable plaza with green space, lighting, trees, landscaping including bioswales for stormwater management, and a complete facade update. A workforce training center is planned as the anchor tenant, alongside recruitment of small and minority-owned businesses.

The renovation is funded through $1.5 million in federal community project funds secured by U.S. Rep. Marcy Kaptur, a $1 million carryover in Community Development Block Grant funds, a $28,000 grant from the Toledo Community Foundation, and a Department of Energy Enhancement and Innovation Grant. A public arts commission call for integrated site artwork had a May 18, 2026 deadline, signaling the project is in its final pre-completion phase.

**Why it matters:** Commercial corridor rehabilitation in legacy neighborhoods like Englewood mirrors the same thesis driving Vibrancy grants elsewhere in Toledo — federal and municipal anchor investment unlocks private tenant recruitment and neighborhood confidence. The workforce training center anchor is the highest-leverage piece: it seeds daily foot traffic independent of retail sales cycles and binds the site to workforce-development partners across the city. If Swayne Field's tenant mix stabilizes around the training center plus minority-owned storefronts, it becomes a replicable model for Toledo's other aging shopping plazas along Detroit, Alexis, and Sylvania Avenues that haven't seen recapitalization in decades.

**Sources:** [The Blade — Shopping center renovation anchors growth in Toledo's Englewood neighborhood](https://www.toledoblade.com/local/city/2026/05/26/shopping-center-renovation-anchors-growth-toledos-englewood-neighborhood/stories/20260526083) · [City of Toledo — Englewood Neighborhood Revitalization Strategy Area](https://toledo.oh.gov/residents/neighborhoods/revitalization/neighborhood-revitalization-strategy-areas/englewood-neighborhood-revitalization-strategy-area)

Held its grand opening Saturday, May 16, in the Gardner Building on Madison Avenue.

FilmToledo — the nonprofit organization supporting film production in northwest Ohio — is opening its first permanent office at 500 Madison Ave, Suite 201, in the Gardner Building (at the corner of Madison Avenue and Superior Street) in early June 2026. ### ProMedica / Medical Mutual network dispute — resolved with new multi-year agreement (November 2025)
_Source: 2025-11-14_

ProMedica and Medical Mutual finalized a new multi-year network participation agreement on November 14, 2025, ending a months-long dispute that had threatened to remove ProMedica from Medical Mutual's in-network provider list for the Toledo area. The agreement applies to all Medical Mutual and Medical Mutual-Paramount insurance products, including employer-sponsored health plans, commercial insurance, ACA marketplace plans, and Medicare Advantage. ProMedica remains in-network for all affected members.

The dispute originated in mid-2025 when Medical Mutual notified members that ProMedica could be dropped if a new contract was not reached before 2026. The November 14 resolution — reported simultaneously by 13abc, The Blade, and WTOL — closed that risk before it materialized. The story is closed out as of May 31, 2026.

**Why it matters:** ProMedica is one of downtown Toledo's largest employers and a anchor of the city's healthcare economy. The resolution removes insurance-network turbulence as a workforce-attraction headwind — employees of Toledo's employers who carry Medical Mutual coverage can access ProMedica facilities without navigating out-of-network costs.

**Sources:** [13abc — ProMedica, Medical Mutual/Paramount finalize agreement (Nov. 14, 2025)](https://www.13abc.com/2025/11/14/promedica-medical-mutualparamount-finalize-agreement/) · [The Blade — ProMedica remains in-network for Medical Mutual, Paramount customers (Nov. 14, 2025)](https://www.toledoblade.com/news/medical/2025/11/14/promedica-finalizes-agreement-medical-mutual-paramount/stories/20251114128) · [WTOL — ProMedica finalizes deal with Medical Mutual to continue in-network access for thousands of patients](https://www.wtol.com/article/news/health/medical-mutual-promedica-finalize-deal-network-access-patients/512-85f16b8c-0ca1-4928-bfb8-bab1ee1e24c5) · [WTOL — Medical Mutual may drop ProMedica as in-network provider (original dispute reporting)](https://www.wtol.com/article/news/local/promedica-medical-mutual-network-dispute-2026-coverage-warning/512-97998a5c-f2ee-497c-ac7c-a3bb0ea66eb5)


### Volunteer group proposes Toledo Sports Commission — modeled on Indianapolis and Cleveland to attract tournaments and visitors
_Source: 2026-05-31_

A volunteer-led group is proposing the creation of a Toledo Sports Commission — a centralized organization designed to attract sporting events, tournaments, and visitors to the region, generating economic impact through sports tourism. WTOL's 'Leading Edge' program reported the initiative on May 31. Proponent Bruce Rump is modeling the proposal on two successful precedents: Indiana Sports Corp., launched in Indianapolis in 1979, attracted more than 450 national and international events and generated an estimated $4 billion in economic impact for the region; the Greater Cleveland Sports Commission has attracted more than 260 events and generated more than $1 billion in impact over 25 years.

Sports tourism consultant Dave Nolan — who helped launch the Greater Cleveland Sports Commission — is advising the Toledo effort. Nolan believes Toledo's niche is amateur and youth sports: soccer, lacrosse, pickleball, running events, figure skating, and youth tournaments, rather than competing with larger cities for professional franchises or marquee events. Governance, funding, and long-term priorities are not yet established. Most participants today are volunteers. No formal entity has been incorporated and no city council resolution has been filed.

**Why it matters:** A Toledo Sports Commission would give regional sports organizers, venues, and local government a single coordination point for event bidding and visitor recruitment — a function that has been notably absent during the planning phases for both the proposed soccer stadium and the RAISE/Uptown design process. Toledo already has Glass City Center, Fifth Third Field, and a growing riverfront park infrastructure; the missing piece is the organizational capacity to convert that venue inventory into a competitive bidding pipeline for national amateur events. Indianapolis and Cleveland built their sports-economy identities around precisely this institutional scaffolding. Whether this proposal advances from volunteer conversations to a funded organization is the first real test of whether Toledo's leadership will treat sports tourism as a line-item economic development strategy.

**Sources:** [WTOL — Can sports help reshape Toledo? New commission looks to Indianapolis and Cleveland for a roadmap](https://www.wtol.com/article/news/local/leading-edge/can-sports-help-reshape-toledo-new-commission-looks-to-indianapolis-and-cleveland-for-a-roadmap/512-d7d86b14-dd41-45bb-b02c-c7d7314f24e7) · [WTOL Leading Edge — Group proposes Toledo sports commission (May 31)](https://www.wtol.com/video/news/local/leading-edge/leading-edge-group-proposes-toledo-sports-commission-return-of-american-white-pelican-may-31/512-eb82aa9e-3f80-46a7-a795-d01303d84938)


### Glass City Riverwalk hits 50% complete — Watershed Weekend June 11–14 will mark the halfway milestone
_Source: 2026-03-25_

Metroparks Toledo has scheduled a four-day celebration June 11–14 along Glass City Riverwalk to mark the halfway point of the 10-year, $250M project, which now connects six Toledo neighborhoods along the Maumee River. The weekend opens June 11 at The Bend — the new elevated trail behind One SeaGate linking the Riverwalk to the MLK Bridge bike/ped lane. Saturday's River Crossing Expo will close the MLK Bridge to motor traffic for rock climbing, paddling, mountain biking and outdoor-skills demos. The weekend also includes an Art Loop anchored by Starburst (a 15-foot illuminated sculpture), the TECHLEDO electronic music festival at The Ribbon and Market Hall, an international vendor fair, and a 5K with BRB Run Club.

The 50% completion marker is more than a programming hook — the Riverwalk is the spine of every other downtown-adjacent investment thesis the city is selling: Glass City Metropark, the future Vistula Metropark, the proposed Vistula soccer stadium, Owens Corning's new 30-year commitment, the East-side urban campground, and Crane Development's Warehouse District buildout all sit within (or are marketed against) this connective tissue. First half completes this summer; full build wraps 2032.

With Watershed Weekend seven days out, 13abc reported June 3 that the Riverwalk's latest completed sections include the former International Park site — now incorporated into Glass City Metropark — and new trail and public-space improvements along the downtown riverfront between Cherry Street and Swan Creek. The event schedule includes the first official lighting of the MLK Bridge on Friday, June 12, and the River Crossing Expo closing the bridge to motor traffic on Saturday, June 13. Metroparks confirmed that Vistula Metropark — its planned 20th park — is targeted to open by 2028, Metroparks Toledo's centennial year.

Destination Toledo confirmed a pro soccer exhibition featuring Toledo Villa FC — the Toledo region's USL League Two pre-professional club — on Friday, June 12, at a temporary field in Vistula sited adjacent to the Toledo Public Schools Administration Building along a future Glass City Riverwalk connection. The match adds soccer programming to the Vistula riverfront during the same weekend that includes the MLK Bridge lighting — and places visible soccer activity near the site of the proposed USL Championship stadium that Summit Street Sports is advancing.

Watershed Weekend is now 4 days out. The full program of nearly 40 free events remains scheduled as of June 7. The Old West End Festival mass shooting on June 6 — in which 12 people were shot and Sunday's events cancelled — adds a public safety backdrop to Toledo's summer outdoor events season. No adjustments to the Watershed Weekend schedule have been announced as of this brief; organizers, Metroparks Toledo, and the city have not issued public statements connecting the OWE incident to Watershed Weekend security planning. Turnout on June 11–14 will be watched as the leading public signal of whether Toledo's outdoor-event confidence absorbs the OWE shooting or contracts around it.

Watershed Weekend opens Thursday June 11, now 2 days away. In direct response to the OWE shooting, Metroparks Toledo announced its most extensive security plan to date — a multi-agency posture involving the Toledo Police Department, Lucas County Sheriff's Office, private security contractors, and Metroparks' own internal police force. Metroparks made the announcement publicly via social media. On Tuesday morning, Mayor Kapszukiewicz, Toledo City Council, and Toledo Police held a joint press conference at One Gov Center to detail a citywide summer safety and youth engagement strategy. The full event schedule remains intact; turnout Thursday will be the first live test of whether the security posture restores public confidence.

Watershed Weekend is now 1 day away, opening June 11. A Watershed Weekend Kickoff Press Conference is scheduled for the morning of June 11 at The Bend. The full program of nearly 40 events, the June 12 MLK Bridge lighting, the June 13 River Crossing Expo road closure, the Toledo Villa FC pro soccer exhibition, and the TECHLEDO music festival at The Ribbon all remain on schedule. The backdrop: as of June 10, no arrests have been made in the OWE festival shooting; two suspects at large, nine victims home from hospital. Toledo's public safety credibility rides on the visible posture and the attendance data that begins to emerge June 11.

Watershed Weekend opened on June 11 with the Rise and Rally supporters kickoff at The Bend behind One SeaGate at 11 a.m., drawing community leaders and Metroparks supporters for remarks marking the Glass City Riverwalk's 50% milestone. The evening program includes the Art Loop: Starburst unveiling — debut of a 15-foot illuminated sculpture — at International Cove from 5 to 9 p.m., followed by Party in the Park at Promenade Park and the first official lighting of the MLK Bridge at 9:45 p.m. The multi-agency security posture is in place for all events. Separately, on the morning of June 11, Toledo Police issued an arrest warrant for Ka Nye Taylor, 20, in connection with the OWE shooting — the first named suspect in the five-day investigation. Opening-day attendance data will begin to emerge through evening social coverage and media reports.

Watershed Weekend Day 2, June 12: tonight's headline event is the first official lighting of the Martin Luther King Bridge — the evening culmination of Party in the Park at Promenade Park, which features multiple bands and a hot-air balloon glow on both sides of the Maumee River. The Toledo Villa FC pro soccer exhibition is underway today at the temporary Vistula field adjacent to the Toledo Public Schools Administration Building — activating the Vistula riverfront corridor and placing visible soccer programming adjacent to the proposed USL Championship stadium site during Toledo's highest-traffic public weekend of the summer. A second major OWE shooting development coincides: Eljay Crisp-Carr, 20, was arrested June 11 — the first arrest in the investigation — which may reduce public anxiety heading into the bridge-lighting crowd. River Crossing Outdoor Expo closes the MLK Bridge to motor traffic tomorrow, June 13, from noon to 4 p.m., for rock climbing, paddling, mountain biking, and outdoor skills demonstrations.

Watershed Weekend Day 3, June 13: The Toledo Blade reported that nearly 500 people attended Thursday's Rise and Rally kickoff at The Bend — a strong opening-day figure given the post-OWE shooting climate. The first official MLK Bridge lighting on Friday evening proceeded as scheduled with no reported security incidents. Today's River Crossing Outdoor Expo (noon–4 p.m.) closes the MLK Bridge to motor traffic in what will be the most visible crowd-draw of the weekend — the first time pedestrians, cyclists, and families have taken over the span since the Riverwalk's 50% milestone was reached. Metroparks, TPD, Lucas County Sheriff, and private security maintain the multi-agency posture through Sunday's closing 5K. Through Day 2, the public confidence test is tracking positive: the event is proceeding as planned, attendees are showing up, and no incidents have been reported.

Watershed Weekend Day 4, June 14 — closing day: The four-day event concludes with the BRB Run Club Inaugural Anniversary 5K (9:00–11:00 a.m.) along the Glass City Riverwalk. Through three full days, no security incidents were reported at any Watershed Weekend venue; the multi-agency posture of TPD, Lucas County Sheriff, private security, and Metroparks' own police force held throughout. In a separate incident overnight June 12–13, three men were shot at the intersection of North Erie Street and Monroe Street in downtown Toledo — approximately one mile from Promenade Park — with non-life-threatening injuries and no suspects identified as of this brief; that shooting is unrelated to Watershed Weekend events or venues. Final cumulative attendance figures are expected from Metroparks after the closing 5K. If Sunday's numbers track the strong opening-day pace — nearly 500 attended Thursday's Rise and Rally alone — Watershed Weekend will close as the clearest public signal that Toledo's outdoor-event confidence held through the OWE shooting and the broader summer safety backdrop.

Watershed Weekend concluded on June 14 with the BRB Run Club Inaugural Anniversary 5K along the Glass City Riverwalk, closing out a four-day program that ran without a single reported security incident across all venues. The multi-agency posture of TPD, Lucas County Sheriff, private security, and Metroparks' own police force held throughout. Metroparks Toledo had not released final cumulative attendance figures as of June 15; the opening-day Rise and Rally kickoff drew approximately 500 people, with consistent social and media coverage indicating strong turnout at the MLK Bridge lighting, the River Crossing Outdoor Expo road closure, and the closing 5K. The public-confidence test that had framed the entire event — could Toledo execute a major outdoor weekend in the immediate aftermath of the OWE mass shooting, with two suspects still at large? — has now closed with a clear answer: yes. That result is the soft-infrastructure milestone Toledo's downtown investment narrative most needed for the summer of 2026.

**Why it matters:** This is the single most consequential piece of soft infrastructure shaping Toledo's downtown thesis. The halfway celebration converts a 10-year construction story into a public-facing brand moment and locks in private-investor confidence for the second half of the build. Anyone making placement decisions in Vistula, the Warehouse District, or East Toledo should plan to be visibly present. Strong turnout will accelerate the next round of Riverwalk-adjacent land assemblies; weak turnout will trigger a quieter pivot back to construction-milestone reporting.

### Sarnie's deli returns to downtown Toledo — reopens at 614 Adams St. in former Fowl Fodder space
_Source: 2026-06-20_

Sarnie's, the downtown Toledo deli that closed during the COVID-19 pandemic, has reopened at 614 Adams St. in the Hylant building — the former Fowl Fodder space — bringing homemade breakfasts, deli sandwiches, and chopped salads back to the downtown lunch circuit. The Blade covered the reopening on June 20. Owner Gareth Jones, who also had a location at Levis Commons in Perrysburg before that closed, has said the focus remains on quality fresh food at a reasonable price. The Adams Street address puts Sarnie's directly in the orbit of the downtown government and office cluster.

The reopening is a small but genuine signal for downtown Toledo's food-and-beverage recovery: a brand with local recognition returning to a street-level location rather than a food hall or ghost kitchen model. 614 Adams St. is within walking distance of Toledo City Hall, the Lucas County government center, and the emerging Huron Yards corridor — a daytime lunch catchment area that has been undersupplied since the pandemic-era closures thinned the downtown dining roster.

**Why it matters:** Each returning downtown anchor — restaurant, gallery, service — adds a data point to the argument that the city's residential and office investments are producing the foot traffic that sustains street-level retail. Sarnie's is not a category-one investment, but its return to a brick-and-mortar Adams Street location after a pandemic-forced closure follows the same logic as Swanky Scoops in the Warehouse District: legacy brands coming back to Toledo's core are the leading indicator of rising commercial confidence, not just new-to-market names. Watch whether Sarnie's draws the daytime office population that will validate similar operator decisions on the same corridor.

**Sources:** [The Blade — Back in business: Sarnie's opens up shop in downtown Toledo](https://www.toledoblade.com/a-e/food/2026/06/20/sarnie-s-deli-back-business-shop-downtown/stories/20260621037) · [WTOL — Sarnie's Deli returns after nearly five years](https://www.wtol.com/video/news/local/sarnies-deli-returns-after-nearly-five-years/512-9544d2c2-a6b9-4f51-b158-3b1ec0d7e9db)


### 5th annual Glass City JazzFest announces August 14–15 lineup at Toledo Zoo Amphitheater and Glass City Metropark
_Source: 2026-07-01_

The 5th annual Glass City JazzFest announced its 2026 lineup on July 1. The two-day festival returns August 14–15: the evening of August 14 at the Toledo Zoo Amphitheater (6–10:30 p.m.; $10 advance, $20 advance reserved, $20 day-of general admission), followed by a free all-day session August 15 at Glass City Metropark (1–10:30 p.m.), the signature riverside venue on the Glass City Riverwalk corridor. TARTA operates transit service to the event.

The dual-venue format places a ticketed cultural draw at the Toledo Zoo and a zero-barrier crowd day at Glass City Metropark on the same mid-August weekend. The Metropark's free day is the economic activation element: it brings thousands of visitors to the riverfront without a ticket price threshold, generating foot traffic for the Maumee riverside restaurants and vendors who rely on high-visibility summer Saturdays to anchor their revenue base.

**Why it matters:** Now in its 5th year, Glass City JazzFest is one of the Metropark system's most established mid-summer events and a direct test of the 'completed Riverwalk section as event attractor' thesis. Free attendance at Glass City Metropark on August 15 creates a no-barrier crowd day for the riverfront that supports the foot-traffic arguments Toledo EDOs and mixed-use developers near the corridor use in their investment cases. The dual-venue model — pairing a ticketed evening at the Zoo Amphitheater with a free riverfront day — also demonstrates the Metroparks-Toledo Zoo programming partnership maturing as a regional event-calendar anchor.

**Sources:** [13abc — 5th annual Glass City JazzFest announces 2026 lineup](https://www.13abc.com/2026/07/01/5th-annual-glass-city-jazzfest-announces-2026-lineup/) · [Glass City JazzFest — official site](https://glasscityjazzfest.com/) · [TARTA — Glass City JazzFest transit service](https://tarta.com/community/events/glass-city-jazzfest/)


### Dough & Co PizzAria opens at 329 N. Huron St. — eighth operator at a revolving downtown address, first one who owns the building
_Source: 2026-07-04_

Dough & Co PizzAria has opened at 329 N. Huron St. in downtown Toledo, becoming the eighth restaurant to occupy the address since 2000. The Blade reported July 4 on the opening; WTOL also covered the location's history of turnover and owner Tyler Scherting's bet on the Four Corners district's momentum. Scherting's approach differs from prior operators in one material way: he bought the building rather than leasing it, giving him a long-term stake in the neighborhood's success rather than a tenant relationship with a landlord. The menu centers on artisan-style pizzas made with 72-hour cold-fermented dough, house-made sauces, and fresh ingredients, with plans to expand offerings over time.

The location at 329 N. Huron St. sits one block from Fifth Third Field and within the corridor that includes Crane Development's Huron Yards, the under-construction Okun Market grocery, and the Four Corners mixed-use district anchored by the Huntington Center. Prior operators at 329 N. Huron included Hamburger Mary's, Poco Piati, and Diva. Scherting acknowledged the address's reputation in both The Blade and WTOL coverage, framing it as opportunity rather than warning: hundreds of apartments coming online nearby and proximity to Huntington Center and Fifth Third Field create a foot traffic floor that earlier operators did not have.

**Why it matters:** A restaurant operator who buys rather than rents signals a different confidence threshold than a tenant — ownership is a longer-term commitment to the block. The Four Corners / Huron Street corridor is the most active sub-district in downtown Toledo's current activation cycle: Okun Market is under construction at 33 N. Huron St., Huron Yards lofts are leased, and the planned apartment supply adjacent to Fifth Third Field has been the primary foot-traffic thesis for operators in the stretch. Dough & Co is a small-ticket story on its own, but it's the eighth data point at a single address — and the first one where the operator is a property owner rather than a renter.

**Sources:** [The Blade — New slice on the block: Dough & Co PizzAria joins downtown Toledo community](https://www.toledoblade.com/a-e/food/2026/07/04/new-slice-block-dough-co-pizzaria-joins-downtown-toledo-community/stories/20260705015) · [WTOL — New pizzeria bets on downtown Toledo address where restaurants have repeatedly come and gone](https://www.wtol.com/article/news/local/new-pizzeria-bets-on-downtown-toledo-address-where-restaurants-have-repeatedly-come-and-gone/512-ebfc4fa0-9420-47d5-822c-80d30636e55b)


### UToledo renews APLU Innovation & Economic Prosperity designation — Glass Innovation Hub anchors $284M regional impact strategy
_Source: 2026-07-09_

The University of Toledo received renewed recognition from the Association of Public and Land-grant Universities (APLU) under its Innovation & Economic Prosperity (IEP) Universities designation program, reflecting UToledo's deepened commitment to regional economic engagement. UToledo president Dr. James Holloway anchored the announcement around the university's 'University for Toledo' identity — explicitly aligning research, talent development, and community partnership to improve the social, cultural, and economic vitality of Northwest Ohio. The announcement was published July 7 by APLU and July 9 by UToledo News. Central to the renewed commitment is UToledo's stewardship of the $31.3 million Glass Innovation Hub, a state-funded initiative co-led with Bowling Green State University that NOIC projects will generate a $284 million regional economic impact, 1,600 new jobs, and $25 million in additional tax revenue over seven years.

The Glass Innovation Hub dedicates $8 million of its $31.3 million budget specifically to talent development: K-12 STEM camps, expanded co-ops and internships, new coursework in glass science and engineering, and graduate and postdoctoral training aligned with industry needs. Toledo's historic glass-industry anchors — Owens Corning, Owens-Illinois, Libbey Glass, NSG/Pilkington, and Guardian Glass — form the demand side of the talent pipeline the Hub is building. The APLU IEP designation tracks university performance across research commercialization, startup formation, licensing revenue, and community-engaged scholarship; UToledo's renewal reflects demonstrated progress across those dimensions in the period since its prior designation.

**Why it matters:** Toledo's site-selector pitch increasingly rests on the intersection of established industry — glass, automotive, advanced materials — and an emerging talent ecosystem that can sustain those industries through their next transformation. UToledo's Glass Innovation Hub is the most direct institutional mechanism for closing that gap: it links the region's century-old industrial identity to workforce curricula, co-op pipelines, and K-12 STEM pathways that convert historic strength into durable competitive advantage. The APLU IEP designation signals external validation of UToledo's regional anchor strategy, and the projected 1,600 jobs and $284M impact — while long-horizon — represent a concrete north star for university-community alignment at a scale Toledo EDOs can cite in site-selector conversations.

**Sources:** [APLU — University of Toledo Advances Regional Prosperity Through Renewed Commitment to Economic Engagement (July 7, 2026)](https://www.aplu.org/news-and-media/blog/2026/07/07/university-of-toledo-advances-regional-prosperity-through-renewed-commitment-to-economic-engagement/) · [UToledo News — University of Toledo Advances Regional Prosperity Through Renewed Commitment to Economic Engagement (July 9, 2026)](https://news.utoledo.edu/index.php/07_09_2026/university-of-toledo-advances-regional-prosperity-through-renewed-commitment-to-economic-engagement) · [BGSU — BGSU, UToledo to serve as lead academic partners on $31.3 million Glass Innovation Hub (2024)](https://www.bgsu.edu/news/online-media-newsroom/2024/07/bgsu-utoledo-to-serve-as-lead-academic-partners-on-innovation-hub-poised-to-strengthen-Ohio-economy-create-jobs.html)
